فصل في الأسآر وغيرها
(۳۳) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ مَوْلَدُهُمَا وَمَأْخَذُهُمَا وَاحِدًا يَأْخُذُ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمَ
ترجمہ : جب کسی شی کی جائے پیدائش اور ماخذ ایک ہو تو حکم بھی دونوں کا ایک ہوگا۔ تشریح : اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب دو چیزیں ایک ہی جگہ سے پیدا ہوتی ہوں تو دونوں کا حکم یکساں ہوتا ہے ، جیسے صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کی وضاحت کی ہے کہ ہر جاندار کے پسینہ کو اس کے سور پر قیاس کیا جائے گا، یعنی جو حکم سؤر کا ہو گا وہی اُس کے پسینہ کا ہو گا، اس لئے کہ پسینہ اور لعاب دونوں گوشت سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں اور اصول ہے کہ جب دو چیزیں ایک ہی جگہ سے پیدا ہوں تو دونوں کا حکم یکساں ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں پر پسینہ اور لعاب کا حکم بھی یکساں ہوگا۔
السبب الظاهر لموت الفأرة الواقعة في البئر وهو الوقوع فى الماء فيحال أى فصار الحكم وهو نجاسة الماء (به) أى بالموت عليه) أى الوقوع، وإن احتمل أن يكون الموت بغيره؛ لأن السبب الموهم لا يضر في مقابلة السبب الظاهر كمن رأى إنسانا في عنقه حية ملفوفة يغلب على الظن أنها نهشته فقتلته كذا ذكره شمس الأئمة الكردري، وكمن جرح إنسانا فلم يزل صاحب فراش حتى مات، فإن الموت يضاف إلى الجرح، وإن احتمل أن يكون بسبب آخر كذا فى المبسوط " ، وكذا لو وجد قتيل في محل يضاف القتل إلى أهلها ، وإن احتمل أنه قتل فى محل آخر ثم حمل إليها.
[البناية: كتاب الطهارة، فصل فى البئر ، ج ۱ ص ۴۶۲، ط: دار الكتب العلمية وَلَانَ لِلْمَوْتِ سَبَبًا ظَاهِرًا وَهُوَ الْوُقُوعُ فِى الْمَاءِ فَيُحَالُ بِالْمَوْتِ عَلَيْهِ وَعَدَمُ الانْتِفَاخِ فِي الْمَاءِ دَلِيلُ قُرْبِ الْعَهْدِ فَقَدَّرَ بِيَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ وَالانْتِفَاحُ دَلِيلُ التَّقَادُمِ فَقُدِّرَ بِالثَّلَاثِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ مَنْ دُفِنَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ فَإِنَّهُ يُصَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ إِلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ وَلَا يُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ لأَنَّهُ يَنَفَشَخُ الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الطهارة، ج ١ ص ۱۹، ط: المطبعة الخيرية
الهداية كتاب الطهارات، فصل فى الآسار، ج ۱ ص ۴۳، ط: رحمانیه لأنَّ السُّورَ مُخْتَلِطٌ بِاللُّعَابِ، وَهُوَ وَالْعَرَقْ مُتَوَلَّدَانِ مِنْ اللَّحْمِ إِذْ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا رُطُوبَةٌ بِهِ =
البحر الرائق: كتاب الطهارة، بول ما يؤكل لحمه ج ۱ ص ۱۳۲، ط: دار الكتاب الاسلامي] (وَعِرُقَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ كَسُورِهِ أَى حُكْمُ اللُّعَابِ وَالْعِرْقِ وَاحِدٌ لِأَنَّ كُلَّا مِنْهُمَا مُتَوَلَّدٌ مِنْ اللَّحْمِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ عِرْقُ كُلِّ حَيَوَان بِسُورِهِ طَهَارَةً وَنَجَاسَةً وَكَرَاهَةٌ.
مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الطهارة ، ج ۱ ص ۳۶، ط: دار إحياء التراث]
If someone died due to some other cause. Its author. Chapter on left-overs (Asar) etc. (33) When a thing and its origin and source are one, one of them takes the ruling of the other. Translation: When the place of origin and source of something is one, then the ruling of both will be one. Explanation: The gist of this is that when two things originate from the same place, their ruling is the same. For example, the author of Hidayah has clarified that the sweat of every living being will be analogized to its flesh. That is, whatever ruling applies to the flesh will apply to its sweat, because sweat and saliva both originate from flesh, and the principle is that when two things originate from the same place, their ruling is the same. Therefore, here the ruling of sweat and saliva will also be the same. The apparent cause of the death of the mouse falling into the well is its falling into water, so the death is attributed to it, and the ruling (of the water being impure) is based on it, even if it is possible that death was due to something else, because a doubtful cause does not harm in the presence of an apparent cause, like one who sees a person with a snake coiled around his neck, and it is strongly presumed that it bit and killed him, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari. And like one who wounds a person and he remains bedridden until he dies, then death is attributed to the wound even if it is possible that it was due to another cause, as in al-Mabsut. Similarly, if a slain person is found in a locality, the killing is attributed to its inhabitants even if it is possible that he was killed elsewhere and then brought there. [Al-Binayah: Book of Taharah, Chapter on the Well, vol. 1 p. 462, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah: And because death has an apparent cause, which is falling into water, so death is attributed to it, and the absence of bloating in water is evidence of recent death, so it is estimated as one day and night, while bloating is evidence of old death, so it is estimated as three. Do you not see that one who is buried before prayer over him, prayer is performed over his grave up to three days, and not after that because he becomes putrefied? Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, Book of Taharah, vol. 1 p. 19, al-Matba'a al-Khayriyyah. Al-Hidayah, Book of Taharat, Chapter on Asar, vol. 1 p. 43, Rahmaniyyah: Because the saliva is mixed with the flesh, and it and sweat are generated from flesh, each being a moisture emanating from it. Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Book of Taharah, urine of what is eaten, vol. 1 p. 132, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami: And the sweat of everything is like its flesh, that is, the ruling of saliva and sweat is the same because each of them is generated from flesh, so the sweat of every animal is considered according to its flesh regarding purity, impurity, and abomination. Majma' al-Anhar: Book of Taharah, vol. 1 p. 36, Dar Ihya al-Turath.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents the foundational legal principle that things originating from the same source share the same ruling. It begins by stating principle (33) in Arabic: 'When a thing and its origin and source are one, one of them takes the ruling of the other.' The author then provides an Urdu translation and commentary, explaining that this means two things from the same origin have identical rulings. He illustrates this with the example from al-Hidayah: the sweat of a living being follows the ruling of its flesh because both sweat and saliva originate from flesh. The passage then supports this principle with several quotations. First, a long quotation from al-Binayah discusses the case of a mouse falling into a well: even if death might be due to another cause, the apparent cause (falling into water) is sufficient to declare the water impure. This illustrates the broader principle of attributing rulings to apparent causes. Next, a quote from al-Hidayah reiterates that saliva and sweat are both generated from flesh. Then a quote from al-Bahr al-Raiq confirms that sweat and saliva share the same ruling based on their common origin. Finally, a reference from Majma' al-Anhar is given. The overall message is that in Hanafi fiqh, the origin of a substance determines its ruling by way of qiyas (analogy) when the effective cause ('illa) is the same. The mouse well example also establishes a separate but related principle: when a clear apparent cause exists, it is attributed to it over hypothetical alternatives.

Key Terms
مَوْلِد (mawlid): Place of origin; the source from which a thing is generated.
مَأْخَذ (ma'khadh): Source; the origin from which a thing derives.
سُؤْر (su'r): Leftover water (or saliva) in the mouth of an animal; also the remaining water in a vessel after drinking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in this lesson, what is the ruling on the sweat of a cat (whose flesh is not eaten)?
A) Pure, because cats are not naturally impure.
B) Impure, because sweat originates from flesh, which is not eaten and thus impure.
C) Pure, because sweat is a different substance.
D) Impure, but only if the cat is alive.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, substances that originate from a body part take the ruling of that part by way of qiyas.

Taharah — Purification

Attributing a Ruling to the Apparent Cause: The Mouse in the Well
Statement of legal principle with proof from analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school attributes the death of a mouse in a well to the apparent cause of falling into water, even if other causes are possible, and apply this principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
When a clear apparent cause exists, it determines the ruling even if other causes are hypothetically possible.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a well water when a mouse falls in and dies. The key issue is whether the death can be attributed to the fall, making the water impure, even if death might have been caused by something else. The Hanafi school relies on the principle of apparent cause (al-sabab al-zahir). We will analyze the reasoning and its application in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A mouse falls into a well and is found dead. The water may be impure if the death is attributed to the fall.
2
Understand the Apparent Cause Principle
The apparent cause is the fall into water; even if the mouse could have died from something else, the default is to attribute death to the fall.
3
Examine the Supporting Analogies
The text gives examples: a snake coiled around a neck, and a wound leading to death. In both, the apparent cause is taken as the true cause.
4
Apply to the Well Case
Since the apparent cause is the fall, the mouse's death is attributed to it, and the water becomes impure after the mouse dies in it.
5
Note Temporal Estimates
If the mouse is not bloated, death is assumed within a day; if bloated, within three days. This affects whether the water is considered impure retroactively.

Key Terms
سَبَب ظَاهِر (sabab zahir): Apparent cause; the most obvious cause that is legally attributed to an event.
انتفاخ (intifakh): Bloating; swelling of the body indicating decomposition.

According to the apparent cause principle, what is the ruling on the water if a mouse is found dead in a well and it is possible it died from poison before falling?
A) The water is pure because the cause of death is uncertain.

The Principle: Whatever Originates from Pure is Pure
Statement of purity principle with supporting proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle 'ma tawallada min tahirin fahuwa aydan tahir' and explain its proof through qiyas.

Core Idea
What originates from pure flesh is pure – saliva takes the ruling of the flesh.

The Hanafi school holds that the leftover water (su'r) of humans and edible animals is pure, even if the person is junub or a disbeliever. This lesson unpacks the principle underlying this ruling: whatever originates from a pure thing is also pure. We will trace the proof from the sources and understand the qiyas (analogical reasoning) that establishes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its statement
Locate the phrase 'إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّذِ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ' in the source. This is the core principle.
The principle is a concise legal maxim.
2
Understand the scope
Identify what the principle applies to: su'r (leftover water/saliva), saliva, and sweat. All originate from the body.
The principle is used to derive the ruling of these substances.
3
Examine the proof presented
The text uses qiyas: saliva is generated from flesh; flesh of humans and edible animals is pure; therefore, saliva is pure. This is the proof chain.
The proof relies on the purity of the source (flesh).
4
Analyse the qiyas formally
Identify the asl (original case: flesh), far (new case: saliva), and illa (effective cause: generation from flesh). The hukm of purity transfers from asl to far.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
5
Note the authority
Recognize that this principle is from Zahir al-Riwayah, confirmed in al-Hidayah and later texts like al-Bahr al-Raiq.
The ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

(۳۴) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّذِ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ. 0
ترجمہ: جو چیز کسی پاک چیز سے پیدا ہو تو وہ بھی پاک ہوا کرتی ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ کو ایک مثال سے واضح فرمایا ہے کہ آدمی کا جھوٹا پاک ہے خواہ وہ مسلمان ہو یا کافر جنبی ہو یا حائضہ ، اس طرح ان جانوروں کا جھوٹا بھی پاک ہے جن کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہے، جیسے گائے ، بکری، اونٹ وغیرہ، جب ان کا گوشت پاک ہے تو اس سے پیدا ہونے والا لعاب بھی پاک ہو گا۔ اسی مسئلے کے ثبوت پر موصوف نے اصول مذکورہ کو بطور دلیل کے پیش کیا ہے کہ پانی لعاب دہن ملنے کی وجہ سے جھوٹا ہوتا ہے اور لعاب پیدا ہوتا ہے گوشت سے اور ان جانوروں کا گوشت پاک ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ جو چیز کسی پاک چیز سے پیدا ہوتو وہ بھی پاک ہوا کرتی ہے، لہذ العاب بھی پاک ہوگا اور جب لعاب پاک ہے تو جس چیز میں ان کا لعاب مخلوط ہو گا وہ چیز بھی پاک ہوگی۔ = مُتَحَلَّلَةٌ مِنْ اللَّحْمِ فَأَخَذَا حُكْمَهُ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الطهارة، بول ما يؤكل لحمه ج ۱ ص ۱۳۲، ط: دار الكتاب الاسلامي] (وَعِرُقَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ كَسُورِهِ أَى حُكْمُ اللُّعَابِ وَالْعِرْقِ وَاحِدٌ لِأَنَّ كُلَّا مِنْهُمَا مُتَوَلَّدٌ مِنْ اللَّحْمِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ عِرْقُ كُلِّ حَيَوَان بِسُورِهِ طَهَارَةً وَنَجَاسَةً وَكَرَاهَةٌ.
مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الطهارة ، ج ۱ ص ۳۶، ط: دار إحياء التراث]
الهداية: كتاب الطهارات، فصل فى البئر، ج ۱ ص ۴۳، ط: رحمانيه
(قَوْلُهُ : وَسُؤْرُ الْآدَمِيٌّ وَالْفَرَسِ وَمَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ) أَمَّا الْآدَمِيُّ فَلَّانَّ لُعَابَهُ مُتَوَلَّدٌ مِنْ لَحْمٍ طَاهِرٍ، وَإِنَّمَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ لِكَرَامَتِهِ وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْجُنُبِ وَالظَّاهِرِ وَالْحَائِضِ وَالنُّفَسَاءِ وَالصَّغِيرِ وَالْكَبِيرِ وَالْمُسْلِمِ وَالْكَافِرِ وَالذَّكَرِ وَالْأُنْثَى.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الطهارة، ج ا ص ۱۳۳ ، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] (فَيَكُونُ حُكْمُهُ) أَى الْمَاءِ حُكْمَ لُعَابِهِ) فَإِنْ كَانَ لُعَابُهُ طَاهِرًا فَالْمَاءِ طَاهِرٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ نَجِسًا فَالْمَاءُ نَجِسٌ يُنْزَحُ كُلُّهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَشْكُوكًا فَالْمَاءُ مَشْكُوكٌ يُنْزَحُ كُلُّهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَكْرُوهًا فَمَكْرُوهُ فَيُسْتَحَبُّ نَزْحُهُ . وَسُؤْرُ الْآدَمِيِّ الظَّاهِرِ الْفَمِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ جُنُبًا أَوْ حَائِضًا أَوْ نُفَسَاءَ أَوْ صَغِيرًا أَوْ كَافِرًا (ق) سُؤُرُ كُلِّ مَا يُؤْكَلُ كَذَلِكَ) أَى طَاهِرُ الْقَمِ طَاهِرٌ لِأَنَّ لُعَابَهُمْ مُتَوَلَّدٌ مِنْ لَحْم طَاهِرٍ فَيَكُونُ الْمَخْلُوطُ به مثلَهُ.
درر الحكام كتاب الطهارة ، ج ۱ ص ۲، ط: دار إحياء الكتب]
57 Usool e Hidayah Vol 1 (34) Indeed, whatever originates from pure is also pure. Translation: Whatever thing originates from a pure thing, it is also pure. Explanation: The author of Hidayah has clarified the mentioned principle with an example: the leftover (su'r) of a human is pure, whether he is Muslim or disbeliever, junub or menstruating. Similarly, the leftover of animals whose flesh is eaten is pure, like cows, goats, camels, etc. Since their flesh is pure, the saliva generated from it is also pure. To prove this issue, he presented the mentioned principle as evidence: water becomes leftover due to mixing with saliva, and saliva originates from flesh, and the flesh of these animals is pure. And the principle is that whatever originates from a pure thing is also pure. Therefore, saliva will be pure, and when saliva is pure, whatever it mixes with will also be pure. = They are dissolved from flesh, so they take its ruling. Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Book of Taharah, urine of what is eaten, vol. 1 p. 132, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami: And the sweat of everything is like its flesh, that is, the ruling of saliva and sweat is one because each is generated from flesh, so the sweat of every animal is considered according to its flesh regarding purity, impurity, and abomination. Majma' al-Anhar: Book of Taharah, vol. 1 p. 36, Dar Ihya al-Turath. Al-Hidayah: Book of Taharat, Chapter on the Well, vol. 1 p. 43, Rahmaniyyah: (His saying: And the leftover of humans, horses, and what is eaten is pure) As for the human, because his saliva is generated from pure flesh, and it is not eaten only due to his dignity, and there is no difference between junub and tahir, menstruating, postpartum, young, old, Muslim, disbeliever, male, female. Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Book of Taharah, vol. 1 p. 133, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami: (So its ruling) i.e., the water's ruling is the ruling of its saliva. So if its saliva is pure, the water is pure; if it is impure, the water is impure, all of it must be drawn; if it is doubtful, the water is doubtful, all of it must be drawn; if it is abominable, it is abominable, and its drawing is recommended. And the leftover of a human with apparent mouth, whether junub, menstruating, postpartum, young, or disbeliever (Q) The leftover of everything that is eaten is similar (i.e., pure of mouth is pure) because their saliva is generated from pure flesh, so what mixes with it is like it. Durar al-Hukkam: Book of Taharah, vol. 1 p. 2, Dar Ihya al-Kutub.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents principle (34): 'Whatever originates from a pure thing is also pure.' The author gives an Urdu translation and commentary, explaining the application to su'r (leftover water/saliva) of humans and edible animals. The key point is that human saliva is pure regardless of the person's religious or ritual state because it originates from pure flesh (since humans are pure). The same applies to animals whose meat is eaten—their saliva is pure. The author then supports this with multiple quotations. Al-Bahr al-Raiq reiterates that sweat and saliva share the same ruling as the flesh because they are generated from it. Majma' al-Anhar provides additional support. Al-Hidayah explicitly states that the su'r (leftover) of humans, horses, and edible animals is pure, emphasizing no distinction between junub, menstruating, etc. The reasoning is consistent: saliva is generated from pure flesh, so it is pure. Durar al-Hukkam confirms that the ruling extends to water mixed with such saliva. This principle is foundational for determining the purity of water in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'r): Leftover water or saliva in the mouth; also the remaining water in a vessel after drinking.
جُنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
لُعَاب (lu'ab): Saliva or spittle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'Whatever originates from pure is pure', what is the ruling on the sweat of a horse?
A) It is pure because horse meat is pure.
B) It is impure because horses are not typically eaten.
C) It is makruh because of doubt.
D) It depends on the horse's health.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that whatever originates from pure is pure is foundational for determining purity of su'r, saliva, and sweat.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Applying the Principle: Su'r of Humans and Edible Animals
Statement of purity principle with supporting proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle to identify the ruling of su'r for humans and edible animals, and evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Human and edible animal su'r is pure regardless of the person's state or belief.

This lesson focuses on the specific rulings derived from the general principle. We will explore why the su'r of humans (including junub, disbelievers) and edible animals is pure, and contrast the Hanafi view with other schools that differ.

Guided Path
1
Recall the principle
Remember the principle (34): 'Whatever originates from a pure thing is also pure.' This is the foundation for all derived rulings.
2
Apply to humans
Human flesh is pure (though not eaten due to dignity). Therefore, human saliva, sweat, and su'r are pure. No distinction between junub, menstruating, etc.
The Hidayah text explicitly lists these categories.
3
Apply to edible animals
Animals whose flesh is eaten have pure flesh (except pork). Their saliva and su'r are pure. Includes cows, sheep, camels, chickens, etc.
Horses are also included separately.
4
Consider the inclusion of horses
The text includes the horse (al-faras) alongside edible animals. Horse meat is considered permissible in the Hanafi school, so its flesh is pure, hence its su'r is pure.
Other schools may differ on horse meat.
5
Compare with other schools
Some scholars consider the su'r of a junub or disbeliever to be impure. The Hanafi response relies on the principle and the absence of evidence to the contrary.
This ikhtilaf is discussed in the sources.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
The Principle of Purity Through Generation
Establishing the purity of saliva using a general legal principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that 'whatever is generated from pure is pure' to determine the purity of the saliva (su'r) of humans and animals whose meat is eaten.

Core Idea
Saliva is pure because it is generated from pure meat, regardless of the person's state or belief.

This lesson explores a foundational Hanafi legal principle: if a substance is generated from a pure source, it inherits that purity. The classical jurists of Al-Hidayah apply this to human and animal saliva (su'r), ruling it pure because it originates from pure meat. We will walk through the evidence and its universal scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? The leftover water/saliva (su'r) of humans, horses, and animals whose meat is eaten. The ruling: pure (tahir).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The general principle: 'Whatever is generated from pure is pure.' This is a qiyas-based maxim derived from the Shariah.
The principle is stated in Arabic at the beginning of the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the principle apply? Saliva is generated from meat. Since the meat of humans (by honor) and permissible animals is pure, the saliva is also pure.
Human meat is not impure; it is simply not eaten due to dignity.
4
Note the universal scope
Does the ruling change based on the person's state? No. The text explicitly states no difference between junub, menstruating woman, minor, adult, Muslim, disbeliever, male, or female.
The purity of the source (meat) is constant.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab dispute
Is this ruling agreed upon? It is mukhtalaf fih. For example, Imam Malik considers the saliva of dogs pure; others may differ on specific animals.
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّدَ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ. وَفِي الْبَحْرِ الرَّائِقِ: مُتَحَلَّلَةٌ مِنَ اللَّحْمِ فَأَخَذَا حُكْمَهُ. وَفِي مَجْمَعِ الْأَنْهُرِ: سُؤُرُ كُلِّ مَا يُؤْكَلُ كَذَلِكَ أَيْ طَاهِرُ الْفَمِ طَاهِرٌ لِأَنَّ لُعَابَهُمْ مُتَوَلَّدٌ مِنْ لَحْمٍ طَاهِرٍ. وَفِي الْهِدَايَةِ: قَوْلُهُ: وَسُؤْرُ الْآدَمِيِّ وَالْفَرَسِ وَمَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ، أَمَّا الْآدَمِيُّ فَلِأَنَّ لُعَابَهُ مُتَوَلَّدٌ مِنْ لَحْمٍ طَاهِرٍ، وَإِنَّمَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ لِكَرَامَتِهِ، وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْجُنُبِ وَالطَّاهِرِ وَالْحَائِضِ وَالنُّفَسَاءِ وَالصَّغِيرِ وَالْكَبِيرِ وَالْمُسْلِمِ وَالْكَافِرِ وَالذَّكَرِ وَالْأُنْثَى.
Indeed, whatever is generated from something pure is also pure. In Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'It is dissolved from the meat, so it takes its ruling.' In Majma' al-Anhur: 'The leftover of everything whose meat is eaten is likewise—i.e., its mouth is pure, because their saliva is generated from pure meat.' In Al-Hidayah: 'His saying: The leftover of humans, horses, and animals whose meat is eaten is pure. As for humans, because their saliva is generated from pure meat; it is not eaten only due to its honor. There is no difference between the junub and the pure, the menstruating woman, the woman in postpartum bleeding, the minor and the adult, the Muslim and the disbeliever, the male and the female.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This lesson presents a fundamental Hanafi legal principle (qa'ida) and its application to purity rulings. The principle states that any substance generated from a pure source is itself pure. The author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle to justify the ruling that the saliva (su'r) of humans and animals whose meat is eaten is pure. The evidence is that saliva is produced from meat, which is pure in these cases (human meat is not eaten due to human dignity, not impurity). The commentary cites supporting texts from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and Majma' al-Anhur to reinforce that the ruling applies universally: no distinction is made based on gender, age, religion, or state of ritual impurity. The reasoning follows a clear qiyas: the source (meat) is pure, so the derivative (saliva) is likewise pure.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'r): The water left after an animal or human drinks, or the saliva/remnant in the mouth.
مُتَوَلَّد (mutawallad): Generated or produced from something else, sharing its ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'whatever is generated from pure is pure', what is the ruling on the saliva (su'r) of a human who is junub?
A) It is impure because the person is in a state of major impurity.
B) It is pure because the saliva is generated from pure meat.
C) It is impure only if the person is a disbeliever.
D) It is makruh but not impure.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes the purity of saliva on the principle of generation: if the source (meat) is pure, the derivative (saliva) is pure, with no exception based on the person's state.

The Principle of Priority (Bil-Ūlā) in Hanafi Fiqh: Dog Saliva Purification
Explaining the principle of priority and its application to the dispute over washing from a dog's lick.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle of priority (bil-ūlā) and apply it to derive the ruling on washing a vessel licked by a dog.

Core Idea
If a greater impurity requires three washes, the lesser impurity requires it with greater priority.

This lesson introduces a powerful logical tool used by Hanafi jurists: the principle of priority (bil-ūlā). It allows deriving rulings for less severe cases from more severe ones. We'll see how it is applied to the case of dog saliva, contrasting with the Shafi'i position, and understand the Hanafi reliance on the practice of Abu Hurayrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
State the Arabic maxim: 'إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُونَهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأُولَى' — meaning if a ruling applies to something, it applies with even greater force to something lesser.
This is a type of qiyas al-awlawi (a fortiori analogy).
2
Recognize the base case
Identify the agreed-upon ruling: dog urine requires three washes to purify a vessel. This is a matter of consensus among the schools.
The source states 'بِالِاتِّفَاقِ' (by agreement).
3
Apply the priority argument
Since dog saliva is considered less impure than its urine (some scholars, like Imam Malik, even consider it pure), if the more impure urine requires three washes, then the less impure saliva must also require three washes, with greater priority (bil-ūlā).
The logic: if the stronger impurity needs three, the weaker also needs three, because the ruling is based on the existence of impurity, and the weaker case is included in the stronger ruling.
4
Examine the opposing hadith and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school relies on a hadith prescribing seven washes, one with dirt. The Hanafi response is that this hadith was abrogated or is interpreted as recommended, as evidenced by Abu Hurayrah (who narrated it) himself washing only three times.
The principle: when a narrator acts contrary to his narration, it indicates abrogation (naskh) or that the ruling was later relaxed.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is: Hanafis wash three times; Shafi'is wash seven times including once with dirt. This affects daily practice when purifying utensils.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is three washes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُونَهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأُولَى. وَفِي الْهِدَايَةِ: وَلَأَنَّ مَا يُصِيبُهُ بَوْلُهُ يَطْهُرُ بِالثَّلَاثِ أَى بِالِاتِّفَاقِ. وَقَوْلُهُ: فَمَا يُصِيبُهُ سُؤْرُهُ وَهُوَ دُونَهُ لِأَنَّ مَالِكًا يَقُولُ بِطَهَارَةِ سُؤْرِهِ وَلَمْ يَقُلْ أَحَدٌ بِطَهَارَةِ بَوْلِهِ فَإِذَا طَهُرَ بَوْلُهُ بِالثَّلَاثِ فَلَأَنْ يَطْهُرَ سُؤْرُهُ أَوْلَى. وَفِي الْعِنَايَةِ: وَلَنَا مَا رَوَاهُ الطَّحَاوِيُّ بِإِسْنَادِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّهُ يُغْسَلُ مِنْ وُلُوعِ الْكَلْبِ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ وَهُوَ الرَّاوِي لِاشْتِرَاطِ السَّبْعِ، وَعِنْدَنَا إِذَا عَمِلَ الرَّاوِي بِخِلَافِ مَا رَوَى أَوْ أَفْتَى لَا تَبْقَى رِوَايَتُهُ حُجَّةً لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ مِنَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ شَيْئًا فَيَعْمَلَ أَوْ يُفْتِيَ بِخِلَافِهِ إِذْ تَسْقُطُ بِهِ عَدَالَتُهُ فَدَلَّ عَلَى نَسْخِهِ، وَهُوَ الظَّاهِرُ لِأَنَّ هَذَا كَانَ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ حِينَ كَانَ يُشَدِّدُ فِي أَمْرِ الْكِلَابِ، وَيَأْمُرُ بِقَتْلِهَا قَلْعًا لَهُمْ عَنْ مُخَالَطَتِهَا، ثُمَّ تُرِكَ وَهَذَا كَمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَأْمُرُ بِكَسْرِ الْأَوَانِي حِينَ كَانَ يُشَدِّدُ فِي الْخَمْرِ قَلْعًا لَهُمْ عَنْهَا وَحَسْمًا لِمَادَّتِهَا ثُمَّ نَهَى عَنْ كَسْرِ الْأَوَانِي أَوْ تُحْمَلُ السَّبْعُ عَلَى الِاسْتِحْبَابِ، وَيُؤَيِّدُهُ مَا رَوَى الدَّارَقُطْنِي.
Indeed, when something has a ruling, then what is lesser than it enters that ruling with greater priority. In Al-Hidayah: 'And because what is affected by its (the dog's) urine becomes pure with three (washes) by agreement. And his saying: Then what is affected by its saliva, and it is lesser than it, because Malik considers its saliva pure and no one considers its urine pure. So if its urine becomes pure with three, then that its saliva becomes pure is even more priority.' In Al-`Inayah: 'And we have what al-Tahawi narrated with his chain from Abu Hurayrah that he used to wash from the licking of a dog three times, and he is the narrator of the condition of seven. And in our view, when the narrator acts contrary to what he narrated or gives a fatwa contrary, his narration is no longer a proof, because it is not permissible for him to hear something from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and then act or give a fatwa contrary to it, as his uprightness would thereby fall. That indicates its abrogation, and it is apparent because this was at the beginning when he was strict concerning dogs and ordered their killing to deter people from mixing with them. Then it was abandoned. This is similar to what is narrated that he used to order the breaking of vessels when he was strict concerning wine to deter them from it and cut off its source, then he forbade breaking vessels. Or the seven (washes) are interpreted as recommended, and this is supported by what al-Daraqutni narrated.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This lesson presents a logical principle (qa'ida) used to defend the Hanafi position on the purification of a vessel licked by a dog. The principle states that if a ruling applies to something, it applies with even greater force to something of lesser degree. The Hanafi school holds that a dog's saliva necessitates washing the vessel three times. The proof uses a priority argument: dog urine is unanimously considered impure and requires three washes; dog saliva is considered less impure (since Imam Malik considers it pure), so if the more impure urine requires three washes, then the less impure saliva certainly requires three washes. The commentary from Al-`Inayah adds a hadith-based argument: Abu Hurayrah (who narrated the seven-wash hadith) himself washed only three times, indicating the seven-wash rule was abrogated or recommended. The text also provides a parallel with the prohibition of wine and breaking vessels, showing that initial strictness was later eased.

Key Terms
بِالْأُولَى (bil-ūlā): With greater priority or all the more reason; indicates that if a ruling applies to the greater, it applies more to the lesser.
سُؤْر (su'r): The leftover water or saliva of an animal; in this context, specifically the saliva from a dog's mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle of priority (bil-ūlā), why does the Hanafi school rule that a vessel licked by a dog requires three washes?
A) Because dog saliva is more impure than its urine.
B) Because if dog urine (more impure) requires three washes, then saliva (less impure) should also require three.
C) Because the Prophet ordered exactly three washes.
D) Because all scholars agree on three washes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling of three washes for dog saliva is derived via the principle of priority (bil-ūlā) and supported by the practice of Abu Hurayrah.

A Fortiori Principle and Dog's Saliva: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains al-awla principle and applies it to dog saliva dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi a fortiori principle to determine the required number of washes for dog saliva and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on ta'abbud.

Core Idea
If dog urine requires three washes, then dog saliva requires three a fortiori.

This lesson delves into a classic inter-madhhab dispute: how many times must a vessel be washed after a dog licks it? The Hanafi school invokes the logical principle of a fortiori (al-awla) alongside direct hadith evidence to argue for three washes. In contrast, the Shafi'i school treats the number as a ta'abbud (ritual prescription) and extends it to seven. By examining the proofs and responses, you will understand how legal reasoning operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the al-awla principle
Begin by articulating the principle: if something has a ruling, then what is lesser in degree falls under that same ruling a fortiori. This is a form of obvious analogy (qiyas jaliy).
The principle is used by the Hanafis to extend a ruling from a more severe impurity to a less severe one.
2
Apply the principle to dog saliva vs urine
Dog urine is unanimously agreed to require three washes (by consensus of the schools mentioned). Since dog saliva is less impure than urine (as even Malik considers saliva pure), it follows a fortiori that saliva also requires three washes.
The passage references Malik's view that dog saliva is pure, strengthening the a fortiori chain.
3
Examine the hadith evidence for three washes
The Hanafi reliance is on the hadith of Abu Huraira, who narrated both a three-wash and a seven-wash version. Critically, Abu Huraira himself acted upon the three-wash version, which, in Hanafi usul, indicates abrogation of the seven-wash ruling.
The narrator's practice overrides his own narration when there is conflict, as it would compromise his integrity if he acted contrary.
4
Understand the Shafi'i ta'abbud argument
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the number of washes for dog saliva as ta'abbud — a purely ritual matter with no rational cause. He then extends it to all dog impurities (urine, sweat) and even to pigs.
Ta'abbud cannot be extended by qiyas according to the Hanafis, which forms the core of their rebuttal.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and the strength of the positions
The Hanafi response uses multiple points: (1) the narrator's action indicates abrogation, (2) a hadith from al-Daraqutni gives a choice between three, five, or seven, showing seven is not obligatory, and (3) ta'abbud cannot be extended analogically. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is three washes.
The principle of al-awla is reinforced by direct textual evidence, making the Hanafi position robust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُونَهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأُولَى.
الهداية كتاب الطهارات، فصل فى الآسار، ج ۱ ص ۴۴، ط: رحمانيه
وَلَأَنَّ مَا يُصِيبُهُ بَوْلُهُ يَطْهُرُ بِالثَّلاثِ أَى بِالاتِّفَاقِ. وَقَوْلُهُ: (فَمَا يُصِيبُهُ سُؤْرُهُ وَهُوَ دُونَهُ) لأَنَّ مَالِكًا يَقُولُ بِطَهَارَةِ سُورِهِ وَلَمْ يَقُلْ أَحَدٌ بِطَهَارَةِ بَوْلِهِ فَإِذَا طَهُرَ بَوْلُهُ بِالثَّلَاثِ فَلَّانُ يَطْهُرَ سُورُهُ (أَوْلَى).
[العناية: كتاب الطهارة، فصل في الآسار، ج ۱ ص ۱۰۹، ط: دار الفكر] وَلَنَا مَا رَوَاهُ الطَّحَاوِيُّ بِإِسْنَادِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّهُ يُغْسَلُ مِنْ وُلُوعَ الْكَلْبِ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ وَهُوَ الرَّاوِى لِاشْتِرَاطِ السَّبْعِ، وَعِنْدَنَا إِذَا عَمِلَ الرَّاوِى بِخِلَافِ مَا رَوَى أَوْ أَفْتَى لَا تَبْقَى رِوَايَتُهُ حُجَّةً لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ مِنْ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ شَيْئًا فَيَعْمَلَ أَوْ يُفْتِيَ بِخِلَافِهِ إِذْ تَسْقُطُ بِهِ عَدَالَتُهُ فَدَلَّ عَلَى نَسْخِهِ ، وَهُوَ الظَّاهِرُ لِأَنَّ هَذَا كَانَ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ حِينَ كَانَ يُشَدِّدُ فِي أَمْرِ الْكِلابِ، وَيَأْمُرُ بِقَتْلِهَا قَلْعًا لَهُمْ عَنْ مُخَالَطَتِهَا، ثُمَّ تُرِكَ وَهَذَا كَمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَأْمُرُ بِكَسْرِ الْأَوَانِي حِينَ كَانَ يُشَدِّدُ فِي الْخَمْرِ قَلْعًا لَهُمْ عَنْهَا وَحَسْمًا لِمَادَّتِهَا ثُمَّ نَهَى عَنْ كَسْرِ الْأَوَانِي أَوْ تُحْمَلُ السَّبْعُ عَلَى الاسْتِحْبَابِ، وَيُؤَيِّدُهُ مَا رَوَى الدَّارَ قُطْنِي
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِى الْكَلْبِ يَلَعُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ أَنَّهُ يُغْسَلُ ثَلَاثًا أَوْ خَمْسًا أَوْ سَبْعًا فَخَيَّرَهُ وَلَوْ كَانَ السَّبُعُ وَاحِبًا لَمَا خَيَّرَهُ ، ثُمَّ إِنَّ الشَّافِعِيُّ جَعَلَ الْعَدَدَ تَعَبُّدًا فِي وُلُوغِ الْكَلْبِ وَعَدَّاهُ إِلَى الْبَوْلِ وَإِلَى رُطُوبَةٍ أُخْرَى مِنْ الْكَلْبِ وَإِلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ وَالشَّيْءُ إِذَا ثَبَتَ تَعَبُّدًا لَا يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَقَدَّرَهُ أَصْحَابُنَا بِالثَّلَاثِ كَسَائِرِ النَّجَاسَاتِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَاهُ وَلِحَدِيثِ الْمُسْتَيْقِظِ.
The thing if it has a ruling, then what is below it enters that ruling a fortiori. Al-Hidayah: 'And because what its urine touches becomes pure with three washes by agreement. And his saying: (What touches its residual saliva and it is below it) because Malik says its residual saliva is pure and no one says its urine is pure, so when its urine is purified by three, then its residual saliva becomes pure a fortiori.' Al-Inayah: 'And for us is what al-Tahawi narrated with his chain from Abu Huraira that [a vessel] is washed from the licking of a dog three times, and he is the narrator of the condition of seven. And according to us, when a narrator acts contrary to what he narrated or gives a fatwa contrary, his narration is no longer a proof, because it is not permissible for him to hear from the Prophet something and then act or give a fatwa contrary to it, as his integrity falls, indicating its abrogation. And that is apparent because this was in the beginning when he was strict in the matter of dogs and ordered killing them to uproot them from mixing with them, then it was abandoned. And this is like what is narrated that he used to order breaking of vessels when he was strict about wine to uproot them from it and cut off its source, then he forbade breaking of vessels. Or the seven is carried on recommendation, supported by what al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Huraira from the Prophet concerning a dog licking a vessel, that it should be washed three times or five times or seven times, giving him a choice. And if the seven were obligatory, he would not have given him a choice. Then al-Shafi'i made the number an act of worship (ta'abbud) in the licking of a dog and extended it to urine and other moisture from the dog and to the pig. And the thing if it is established as an act of worship, it is not extended to others. And our companions estimated it as three like other impurities due to what we narrated and the hadith of the one who wakes up.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi legal principle (al-awla) and its application to a specific fiqh issue: the purification of vessels contaminated by a dog's saliva. The passage begins by stating the principle: when something has a ruling, anything lesser in degree falls under the same ruling a fortiori. The author then applies this to the case of a dog's saliva versus its urine. The Hanafi school holds that a vessel licked by a dog must be washed three times, based on the hadith of Abu Huraira who narrated three washes and himself acted upon that. The passage then addresses the Shafi'i position, which requires seven washes for dog saliva and extends it to all dog impurities and even to pigs based on ta'abbud (ritual prescription). The Hanafi response is that if it were ta'abbud, it could not be extended to other cases by analogy. The Hanafis instead measure the number of washes to three, similar to other impurities, supported by the hadith from al-Daraqutni giving a choice between three, five, or seven, indicating that seven is not obligatory. The passage also discusses the abrogation of stricter rules regarding dogs, similar to the abrogation of breaking wine vessels.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'r): The residual water or liquid left in a vessel after an animal drinks, or the saliva of an animal that mixes with water.
بِالْأُولَى (bi al-awla): A fortiori; a logical argument that if something applies to a higher degree, it applies more so to a lesser degree.
تَعَبُّد (ta'abbud): A matter of ritual worship that is not based on rational cause ('illa), but on pure obedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on washing a vessel licked by a dog?
A) It must be washed seven times, once with earth.
B) It must be washed three times, based on the a fortiori principle and hadith.
C) It is sufficient to rinse it once.
D) No washing is needed because dog saliva is pure.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the a fortiori principle and the narrator's practice to uphold three washes for dog saliva, while the Shafi'i school treats the number as a fixed ritual requiring seven washes.

Taharah — Purification

The Principle: Whatever is Produced from Impure is Impure
Stating principle and applying to saliva of predatory animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that anything generated from an impure source is impure, and identify which animals' residual saliva is classified as impure based on this principle.

Core Idea
If the source is impure, its product is impure — a key Hanafi principle for deriving purity rulings.

Where does impurity end? The Hanafi school uses a powerful generative principle: anything produced or generated from an impure source takes on its impurity. This lesson explores that principle through the ruling on the su'r (residual liquid) of pigs, dogs, and predatory animals. We will see how the Hanafi school uses both textual evidence (hadith for dogs) and reasoned analogy (qiyas) to establish impurity.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Begin with the general rule: whatever is produced or generated from something impure is itself impure. This is a foundational Hanafi principle in taharah.
Principle: 'Ma tawallada min najisin fahuwa aydan najis.'
2
Identify the three impure su'rs
According to Al-Hidayah, the third category of su'r (residual liquid) is impure: that of the pig, the dog, and predatory animals (siba'). List them clearly.
3
Examine the proof for each
For the pig: it is najis al-'ayn (intrinsically impure) and its saliva is produced from its flesh. For the dog: a hadith orders washing the vessel after its licking, and its tongue contacts the water directly. For predatory animals: their saliva is impure because it is produced from their flesh, which is impure due to their consumption of carrion.
The hadith for dog: 'The Prophet ordered washing the vessel from its licking three times, and in a narration seven times.'
4
Understand the underlying talil
The common reasoning (ta'lil) is that the impurity of the source (flesh) transfers to the product (saliva) through the process of generation (tawallud). This is similar to how milk from an impure animal would be impure.
Analogy: milk from a pig is impure because it is produced from impure flesh.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
The impurity of dog's saliva is agreed upon by Hanafis and Shafi'is, but the number of washes differs (3 vs 7). Maliki school considers dog's saliva pure. Hanafis classify predatory animals' saliva as impure; Shafi'is differ on some predators.
Cross-madhhab: Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih.

Whatever is produced from an impure thing is also impure. Al-Hidayah: 'And the third type is impure, and it is the residual saliva of the pig, dog, and predatory animals. As for the pig, because it is impure in itself and its saliva is produced from its flesh. As for the dog, because the Prophet ordered washing the vessel from its licking three times, and in a narration seven times, and its tongue contacts the water and not the vessel, so it is more deserving of impurity. As for predatory animals, because it contains their saliva, and it is impure due to being produced from impure flesh like milk.' Al-Ikhtiyar: 'As for the impurity of the pig's residual saliva, due to what preceded that it is impure in itself, and as for the residual saliva of predatory animals, because it is produced.'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle that anything generated from an impure source is itself impure, then applies it to classify the su'r (residual liquid) of certain animals. The passage begins by stating the principle, then quotes Al-Hidayah which divides su'r into three categories: pure, pure but disliked, and impure. The third category includes pig, dog, and predatory animals. For the pig, the impurity is intrinsic (najis al-'ayn), and its saliva is produced from its impure flesh. For the dog, the proof is from the hadith ordering washing after its lick, and its tongue directly contacts the water, making its saliva more severely impure. For predatory animals (like lions, wolves, etc.), their saliva is impure because it is produced from their impure flesh, similar to the way milk is produced from an animal's flesh (if the flesh is impure, the milk is impure). The Al-Ikhtiyar quote reaffirms the same reasoning. This principle is used by the Hanafi school to derive rulings on the purity of various liquids originating from impure sources.

Key Terms
سِبَاع (siba'): Predatory animals of the land, such as lions, wolves, bears, etc., that hunt with their claws or fangs.
نَجِسُ الْعَيْن (najis al-'ayn): Intrinsically impure; something whose very substance is impure, like pigs and dogs.
مُتَوَلَّد (mutawallid): Produced or generated from something else; here referring to the origin of saliva from the flesh of the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because its saliva is produced from its flesh, which is impure.
C) Because the Prophet explicitly mentioned all predators.
D) Because predators do not drink water properly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that whatever is produced from an impure source is impure is a foundational tool for determining purity of liquids, especially the saliva of animals whose flesh is impure.

The Principle: What Generates from Impurity is Impure
This passage states a qawida about generation from impurity and applies it to su'r of predatory beasts, dog, and pig, with proof from hadith and qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that what generates from impurity is impure, apply it to determine the ruling of su'r (leftover water) of predatory animals, and explain the Hanafi reasoning against the Shafi'i devotional approach.

Core Idea
The offspring of impurity shares its parent's impurity – meat determines saliva's purity.

Previously, you learned that what originates from pure things is pure. Now we encounter the opposite: if something originates from an impure source, it carries that impurity. This principle is crucial for understanding many rulings in taharah, especially concerning the leftover water (su'r) of animals. This lesson unpacks the qawida, its proof, and its application to predatory beasts, dogs, and pigs, along with a comparison with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
First, locate the principle: 'Whatever is generated from an impure thing is also impure.' Understand that this is a foundational maxim in Hanafi fiqh for derivatives like saliva, milk, and eggs.
The qawida is stated at the beginning of the passage.
2
Apply the Qawida to Predatory Beasts
The author applies the principle to the su'r of predatory beasts (e.g., lion, wolf). The reasoning: their meat is impure, and saliva originates from meat. Therefore, their su'r is impure.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the impurity of the meat.
3
Analyze the Dalil for the Dog
The hadith about a dog licking a vessel requires washing three, five, or seven times. Hanafis interpret the choice as indicating that the number is not devotional but based on customary cleaning. The dog's su'r is impure because its tongue touches the water and its meat is impure (according to Hanafis).
The hadith is from Abu Hurayra; the choice given by the Prophet shows flexibility.
4
Compare with Shafi'i Position
Al-Shafi'i treats the number of washes as a devotional (ta'abbudi) matter and extends it to all dog impurities and pig. Hanafis reject extension because devotional rulings are not analogized. They set the number at three, like other impurities.
This illustrates a methodological difference in usul al-fiqh.
5
Confirm the Ruling for Pig
The pig is impure in itself (najis al-'ayn), so its su'r is impurely straightforwardly, without needing the qawida.
The qawida is used for animals whose impurity is derived, not inherent.

عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِى الْكَلْبِ يَلَعُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ أَنَّهُ يُغْسَلُ ثَلَاثًا أَوْ خَمْسًا أَوْ سَبْعًا فَخَيَّرَهُ وَلَوْ كَانَ السَّبُعُ وَاحِبًا لَمَا خَيْرَهُ ، ثُمَّ إِنَّ الشَّافِعِيُّ جَعَلَ الْعَدَدَ تَعَبُّدًا فِي وُلُوغِ الْكَلْبِ وَعَدَّاهُ إِلَى الْبَوْلِ وَإِلَى رُطُوبَةٍ أُخْرَى مِنْ الْكَلْبِ وَإِلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ وَالشَّيْءُ إِذَا ثَبَتَ تَعَبُّدًا لَا يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَقَدَّرَهُ أَصْحَابُنَا بِالثَّلَاثِ كَسَائِرِ النَّجَاسَاتِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَاهُ وَلِحَدِيثِ الْمُسْتَيْقِظِ. الاختيار لتعليل المختار: كتاب الطهارة، ج ١ ص ۱۹، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
وَأَمَّا نَجَاسَةُ سُورِ الْخِنْزِيرِ فَلِمَا تَقَدَّمَ أَنَّهُ نَجِسُ الْعَيْنِ، وَأَمَّا سُؤُرُ سِبَاعِ الْبَهَائِمِ فَلَانَّهُ مُتَوَلَّدٌ
(36) Verily whatever is generated from an impure thing, it also is impure. Translation: Something that originates from an impure thing is also impure. Explanation: Previously, the author of al-Hidayah mentioned a principle: what originates from a pure thing is pure. But here he mentions a contrary principle: if a thing originates from an impure thing, it will also be impure. He clarifies with an example: in the Hanafi school, the leftover water (su'r) of predatory beasts (lion, leopard, wolf, elephant, etc.) is impure. The reason is that the meat of such beasts is impure, and saliva is generated from it. The principle is: what originates from an impure thing is impure. In determining purity and impurity of saliva, consideration is given to the meat. Since the meat of these beasts is impure, their leftover water (which originates from their meat) is impure. From Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning a dog licking a vessel: that it be washed three times or five times or seven times, and he gave him a choice. Had the number seven been obligatory, he would not have given a choice. Then al-Shafi'i considered the number a devotional matter in the case of a dog's licking, and extended it to urine and other moisture from the dog, and to the pig. But when something is established as devotional, it is not extended to other cases. Our (Hanafi) scholars set the number at three like other impurities, based on what we have narrated and the hadith of the one who wakes up. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Kitab al-Taharah, vol. 1, p. 32, Dar al-Kutub al-Islami] [Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Taharat, Fasl fi al-Athar, vol. 1, p. 44, Rahmaniyya] And the third type is impure: the leftover water of the pig, the dog, and predatory beasts. As for the pig, because it is impure in itself and its saliva is generated from its meat. As for the dog, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded washing the vessel from its licking three times, and in a narration seven times, and its tongue touches the water, so it is more deserving of impurity. As for predatory beasts, because their saliva is impure due to being generated from impure meat, like milk. [al-Ikhtiyar li Ta'lil al-Mukhtar, Kitab al-Taharah, vol. 1, p. 19, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya] As for the impurity of the pig's leftover water, it is due to what preceded: that it is impure in itself. As for the leftover water of predatory beasts, it is because it is generated...
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage from Usool al-Hidayah presents a foundational qawida (legal maxim): anything generated from an impure source is itself impure. The author first contrasts this with a previously stated principle that what originates from pure is pure. He then illustrates with a concrete Hanafi ruling: the su'r (leftover water or saliva) of predatory land animals (such as lions, wolves, and elephants) is impure because their meat is impure. The 'illa (effective cause) is that saliva is generated from flesh, so it takes the ruling of the flesh. The passage also cites the hadith on a dog licking a vessel, where the Prophet gave a choice between washing three, five, or seven times. The Hanafi school uses this hadith to argue that the number is not a devotional matter but based on customary purification, unlike al-Shafi'i who treats the number as devotional and extends it to all dog impurities. The passage then quotes al-Hidayah and al-Ikhtiyar to confirm the ruling: pig's su'r is impure because it is impure in itself, dog's su'r is impure based on the hadith (even though its meat is impure according to Hanafis due to prohibition), and predatory beasts' su'r is impure due to generation from impure flesh. The qiyas here is that just as milk from a pure animal is pure, so saliva from an impure animal is impure. This principle has wide application in taharah (purification) rulings.

Key Terms
متولد (mutawallid): That which originates or is generated from something else.
نجس (najis): Legally impure substance that prevents validity of prayer if present in a certain amount.
سؤر (su'r): The remaining water in a vessel after an animal drinks or the saliva/moisture that mixes with water.
ولغ (walagh): The act of a dog drinking by lapping with its tongue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because lions are predatory and thus inherently impure.
B) Because the lion's meat is impure, and its saliva is generated from that meat.
C) Because the Prophet specifically declared lion's su'r impure.
D) Because lions have no known purification ritual.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the purity of a derivative depends on the purity of its source; thus, the su'r of any animal whose meat is impure is also impure.

Conflicting Evidences on Permissibility and Prohibition Cause Doubt
States a qawida on doubt from conflicting evidence and applies it to donkey's su'r.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida on conflicting evidences causing doubt and apply it to determine the ruling on donkey's su'r as mashkuk.

Core Idea
When evidences for permissibility and prohibition conflict, the ruling becomes doubtful—do not rush to declare haram.

The Hanafi legal tradition recognizes that not every conflict of evidence yields a definitive ruling. When the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Sahaba opinions point in opposite directions regarding halal and haram, the law imposes hesitation (tawaqquf). This lesson examines this principle through the classic case of the domestic donkey's leftover water (su'r), where two hadiths and differing Sahaba views create genuine doubt.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the rule: ta'arud of adilla on ibaha and hurma produces shakk, as does ikhtilaf al-sahaba.
2
Identify the cause of doubt
Recognize that the specific case (donkey's su'r) has two conflicting pieces of evidence: one hadith permits donkey meat, another forbids it.
3
Examine the conflicting proofs
Study the permission hadith (advising to feed family with fat donkeys) and the prohibition hadith (forbidding donkey meat and calling it impure).
4
Determine the Hanafi ruling
Because the evidence is contradictory and not resolvable through tarjih, the su'r is mashkuk (doubtful) – not definitively pure or impure.
5
Apply the consequence: tawaqquf
The practical result: caution is advised; avoid the su'r if possible, but if used, prayer is valid due to the original presumption of purity (istishab).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٣٧) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِى الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالْحُرُمَةِ يُورِثُ الشَّكَ وَكَذَا اِخْتِلافُ الصَّحَابَةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمُ .
ترجمہ: جب ادلہ اباحت اور حرمت متعارض ہو جائیں یا صحابہ کرام کا اختلاف تو اس صورت میں حکم میں شک پیدا ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح: اصول کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب کسی چیز کے مباح اور حرام ہونے میں دلائل متعارض ہو جائیں، یا صحابہ کے درمیان اُس مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو تو شک پیدا ہو جاتا ہے، یقینی طور پر کسی ایک جہت کا فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا ، ایسی صورت میں توقف کیا جائے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ گدھے کے جھوٹے میں شک کے دوسبب ہیں، ایک تو یہ ہے کہ اس کے مباح ہونے اور حرام ہونے میں دلائل مختلف ہیں ، چنانچہ روایت میں ہے کہ غالب بن ایجر نے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے دریافت کیا کہ ہمارے ہاں قحط سالی ہے، میرے پاس ہمارے گھر والوں کو کھلانے کے لئے فربہ گدھوں کے علاوہ کچھ بھی نہیں ہے، اور آپ نے پالتو گدھوں کو حرام قرار دیا ہے، تو آپ نے فرمایا:
أَطْعِمُ أَهْلَكَ مِنْ سَمِيْنِ حُمُرِكَ. ترجمہ: اپنے گھر والوں کو فربہ گدھوں کا گوشت کھلاؤ۔
یہ حدیث گدھے کے گوشت کی حلت پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔
حضرت خالد بن ولید رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے گھوڑے، خچر ، گدھے اور چیر پھاڑ دینے والے درندوں کے گوشت سے منع فرمایا ہے:
= مِنْ لَحْمِهِ وَلَحْمُهُ حَرَامٌ نَجِسٌ. [تبيين الحقائق كتاب الطهارة، ج ۱ ص ۳۲، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الطهارات، فصل فى الآسار، ج ا ص ۴۵، ط: رحمانیه]
سنن أبي داود: كتاب الأطعمة، باب في أكل لحوم الحمر الأهلية، ج ۳ ص ۳۵۶، رقم الحدیث: ۳۸۰۹، ط: المكتبة العصرية ]
(37) Verily the contradiction of evidences concerning permissibility and prohibition causes doubt, and likewise the difference of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them). Translation: When evidences for permissibility and prohibition become contradictory, or when there is difference among the Companions, then the ruling becomes questionable. Explanation: The essence of the principle is that when the evidences for something being permissible or prohibited conflict, or when the Companions differ on that issue, doubt arises, and a definite decision cannot be made; one must pause. The author of al-Hidayah said that the doubt about the leftover water of the donkey has two causes. First, the evidences for its permissibility and prohibition differ. Thus, it is narrated that Ghalib ibn Ajar asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): “We are in famine, and I have nothing to feed my family except fat donkeys, and you have declared domestic donkeys prohibited.” So he said: “Feed your family from your fat donkeys.” This hadith indicates the permissibility of donkey meat. And it is narrated from Khalid ibn al-Walid (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the meat of horses, mules, donkeys, and every beast of prey that has fangs: from its meat, for its meat is forbidden and impure. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Kitab al-Taharah, vol. 1, p. 32] [Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Taharat, Fasl fi al-Athar, vol. 1, p. 45, Rahmaniyya] Sunan Abi Dawud, Kitab al-At'ima, no. 3809.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents another qawida: when there is ta'arud (conflict) between evidences for permissibility (ibaha) and prohibition (hurma), or when the Sahaba (Companions) themselves differed on a matter, the ruling becomes doubtful (shakk). The consequence is that one cannot be certain of either permissibility or prohibition; the law imposes hesitation (tawaqquf). The author applies this to the question of the su'r (leftover water) of donkeys. The doubt arises from two conflicting texts: (1) a hadith where the Prophet permitted eating donkey meat during famine, implying the animal is pure, and (2) a hadith forbidding donkey meat, implying its impurity. Since the Sahaba also differed on this issue (some considered it permissible, others prohibited), doubt is reinforced. Therefore, the Hanafi ruling on donkey's su'r is not one of definite purity or impurity; rather, the matter requires caution. The passage ends with references from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Hidayah. This principle is widely used in Hanafi legal theory when dealing with conflicting evidence from the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Sahaba opinions.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict or contradiction between two evidences in a way that both cannot be simultaneously applied.
دلائل (adilla): Evidences from Shari'ah, typically Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas.
اباحت (ibaha): Permissibility; the legal category of mubah (allowed).
حرمت (hurma): Prohibition; the legal category of haram.
شك (shakk): Doubt, uncertainty about a legal ruling due to conflicting evidence.
اختلاف الصحابة (ikhtilaf al-sahaba): Difference of opinion among the Companions of the Prophet on a legal issue.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment; refraining from declaring a definitive ruling when evidence is conflicting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the leftover water (su'r) of a domestic donkey considered doubtful (mashkuk) in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly said donkey's su'r is impure.
B) Because there are conflicting hadiths on the permissibility of donkey meat, and the Companions differed.
C) Because donkeys are not mentioned in the Qur'an.
D) Because the Hanafi school has no ruling on donkeys.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting evidences on permissibility and prohibition or differences among the Companions produce doubt (shakk) in the ruling, leading to caution (tawaqquf) without definitive assignment of halal or haram.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Conflicting Evidence Creates Doubt: The Case of Donkey's Leftover Water
Illustrating the principle of doubt from conflicting evidence via donkey's su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of the donkey and mule, identify the conflicting evidences that cause doubt, and apply the principle of shakk (doubt) resulting from ta'āruḍ (conflict of proofs).

Core Idea
Conflicting evidences about donkey's meat and Companions' views create doubt, rendering its leftover water mashkūk (doubtful).

The Hanafi legal tradition is built on careful weighing of evidence (tarjih). When evidence is irreconcilably conflicted, certainty cannot be reached, leading to a state of doubt (shakk). This lesson examines a classic case: the leftover water of a donkey. By exploring the conflicting hadiths, divergent Companion opinions, and analogical reasoning, you will understand how the Hanafi school derives a ruling that is neither pure impurity nor full purity, but a cautious middle ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal subject
First, pinpoint what is being discussed: the su'r (leftover water) of the domestic donkey (and mule). Determine whether the ruling concerns purity (tahārah), purificatory power (tahūriyyah), or both.
The passage focuses on the su'r of the donkey; the mule follows by lineage.
2
Locate and list the conflicting proofs (adillah)
Identify the two hadiths: the Khaybar hadith (prohibition, declaring the meat rijs) and the al-Abjar hadith (permission to eat). Also note the conflicting Companion statements (Ibn Abbas vs. Ibn Umar). These create a prima facie conflict (ta'āruḍ).
Both hadiths are ahad (zanni al-thubut), so neither can override the other based on transmission certainty.
3
Examine the qiyas (analytical reasoning)
The author compares the donkey to the dog (ghayr ma'kul al-lahm, implying najasah) and to the cat (domestic, kept in houses, implying taharah). This dual analogy yields contradictory indications, reinforcing the doubt.
The cat's su'r is pure and purifying in the Hanafi school; the donkey shares domesticity but lacks the same level of need (balwā).
4
Identify the three intra-Hanafi views on the doubt
From the conflicting evidence, three positions emerged: (1) doubt in purity (tahārah) only, (2) doubt in purificatory power (tahūriyyah) only, (3) doubt in both. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The passage discusses each view in order of increasing comprehensiveness.
5
State the mufta bihi (operative ruling) and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position considers the su'r as mashkūk: pure (tāhir) but not purifying (ghayr tahūr). This means wudu with it is valid but makruh tanzih, and tayammum is not allowed when this water is available.
This ruling illustrates how doubt leads to caution without prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن تعارض الأدلة فى الإباحة والحرمة يورث الشك وكذلك اختلاف الصحابة رضي الله عنهم. والحمار والبغل مشكوك أي سؤرهما مشكوك فيه. أما الحمار فلتعارض الأدلة؛ لأنه قد ثبت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه أمر يوم خيبر بإكفاء القدور من لحوم الحمر الأهلية وقال إنه رجس. وروي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه قال للأبجر بن غالب حين قال له ليس لي إلا حميرات كل من سمين مالك. وكان ابن عباس يقول كل ما يعتلف القت والتبن فسؤره طاهر. وكان ابن عمر يقول إنه رجس. ولأنه يشبه الكلب من حيث إنه غير مأكول اللحم ويشبه الهرة من حيث إنه يربط في الدور والأفنية. فتعارضت الأدلة فيه فوقوع الشك. ثم قيل الشك في طهارته لما ذكرنا من أنه يشبه الكلب من وجه والهرة من وجه. وقيل في طهوريته لأنه يشبه الهرة من الوجه الذي ذكرنا فيكون طهورا باعتباره، ويفارقها من حيث إنه لا يدخل المضائق ولا يصعد العرف فكان البلوى فيه دونها في الهرة فيخرج من أن يكون طهورا باعتباره فأوجب الشك في الطهورية. وقيل الشك في الطهارة والطهورية جميعا. وأما البغل فهو من نسل الحمار فيكون بمنزلته هكذا.
Indeed, the conflict of evidences regarding permissibility and prohibition causes doubt, and likewise the difference of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. The donkey and the mule are doubtful, i.e., their leftover water (su'r) is doubtful. As for the donkey, due to the conflict of evidences: because it is established from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that on the day of Khaybar he ordered the overturning of pots containing the meat of domestic donkeys and said it is impure (rijs). And it is narrated from him, peace and blessings be upon him, that he said to al-Abjar ibn Ghālib when he said to him, 'I have only donkeys' (to feed my family): 'Eat from your fat ones' (i.e., meat of fat donkeys). And Ibn Abbas used to say: 'Anything that feeds on grass and straw, its leftover water is pure (tāhir).' And Ibn Umar used to say: 'It is impure (rijs).' And because it resembles the dog in that its flesh is not eaten, and it resembles the cat in that it is tied in houses and courtyards. Thus the evidences conflicted regarding it, so doubt occurred. Then it is said the doubt is regarding its purity (tahārah) due to what we mentioned, that it resembles the dog in one aspect and the cat in another. And it is said regarding its purificatory power (tahūriyyah) because it resembles the cat in the aspect we mentioned, so it is purifying (tahūr) in that regard; but it differs from the cat in that it does not enter narrow places nor climb upon roofs, so the need (balwā) for it is less than the need for the cat. Thus it is excluded from being purifying in that regard, so doubt is necessitated regarding its purificatory power. And it is said the doubt is regarding both purity and purificatory power. As for the mule, it is from the progeny of the donkey, so it follows its ruling. Thus.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage from Usool al-Hidayah discusses a foundational legal principle: when evidences conflict regarding permissibility and prohibition, or when the Companions differ on a matter, doubt (shakk) arises. The author applies this principle to the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of the domestic donkey (himār) and mule (baghl). The doubt is not about the animal's permissibility as food—that is settled by the explicit prohibition on domestic donkey meat—but about the purity of its saliva and leftover water. The text presents two conflicting hadiths: one where the Prophet prohibited and declared donkey meat impure, and another where he permitted eating fat donkeys during famine. Additionally, Companions differed: Ibn Abbas held the su'r pure, Ibn Umar held it impure. By analogy, the donkey resembles the dog (non-edible meat, strong impurity) and the cat (domestic animal, often kept). Since the cat's su'r is considered pure and purifying in the Hanafi school, the donkey's similarity to the cat suggests purity, but its dissimilarity (less domestic contact) weakens that claim. This leads to three scholarly views: doubt about its purity (tahārah), doubt about its purificatory power (tahūriyyah), or doubt about both. The mule follows the donkey due to lineage. The final operative ruling in the Hanafi school treats the su'r of donkey and mule as suspect (mashkūk), meaning it should be avoided when possible, but if used, tayammum is not valid (since the water might be impure) yet wudu with it is considered valid but disliked. The passage demonstrates how usul al-fiqh principles (ta'āruḍ, shakk, qiyas) yield nuanced rulings.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water (or any liquid) that remains after an animal drinks from it.
مشكوك (mashkūk): Doubtful; a ruling that cannot be definitively determined due to conflicting evidence.
تعارض (ta'āruḍ): Conflict or contradiction between two or more pieces of evidence (adillah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the cause (sabab) of doubt regarding the su'r of the donkey according to the passage?
A) The donkey's meat is haram to eat.
B) There is conflicting evidence: two contradictory hadiths and differing Companion views.
C) The donkey resembles the dog in being non-edible.
D) The cat's su'r is purifying.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting evidence on a ruling creates a state of doubt (shakk) that does not render the object impure but prevents it from being purifying.

Ruling on Su'r of Donkey and Mule: Mashkuk (Doubtful)
Ruling with proof on su'r of donkey and mule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of donkey and mule, identify the conflicting evidence, and explain why it is classified as mashkuk.

Core Idea
Conflicting proofs on donkey's su'r produce doubt, so Hanafis deem it mashkuk—neither pure nor impure.

The leftover water (su'r) of donkeys and mules is a classic example of how conflicting evidence leads to a unique Hanafi category: mashkuk (doubtful). In this lesson, we explore the primary hadiths, the differing opinions of Companions, and the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that cause this doubt, ultimately arriving at the Hanafi ruling that such water is not to be used for wudu when pure water is available.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling on su'r of donkey and mule: it is mashkuk (doubtful). Explain what mashkuk means in Hanafi fiqh—it is not definitively pure or impure, and using it for wudu is makruh tanzih.
The text explicitly says 'the donkey and mule are doubtful, meaning their leftover water is doubtful.'
2
Identify the conflicting primary sources
Locate the two seemingly contradictory hadiths: the Khaybar hadith where the Prophet ordered pots overturned and called donkey meat 'rijs', and the hadith of Abjar where permission to eat from donkeys was given. Note the Companions' disagreement (Ibn Abbas vs Ibn Umar).
The Khaybar hadith suggests impurity, while the Abjar hadith suggests permissibility.
3
Analyze the qiyas involved
The donkey resembles a dog (not eaten, so su'r could be impure) and a cat (domestic, so su'r could be pure). This double resemblance creates contradictory analogies, strengthening the doubt.
The text states: 'it resembles the dog... and resembles the cat... thus the evidence conflicted.'
4
Examine the three interpretations of doubt
Scholars differed on whether the doubt covers purity (tahara) alone, purifying quality (tahuriyya) alone, or both. Understand the reasoning behind each: resemblance to cat suggests purity, but domestic habits differ from cat, causing doubt in purifying quality.
The text says 'some said the doubt is in its purity... some in its purifying quality... some in both.'
5
Conclude the operative ruling
The mufta bihi position: su'r is mashkuk; it is not to be used for wudu if pure water is available. If used, wudu is valid but makruh tanzih. The mule follows the same ruling due to its lineage from the donkey.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is consider it pure (tahir) but not purifying; Malikis consider it najis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نَهَى عَنْ أَكْلِ لُحُومِ الْخَيْلِ وَالْبِغَالِ وَالْحُمُرِ وَكُلَّ ذِى نَابِ مِنَ الرِّبَاعِ . یہ حدیث گدھے کے گوشت کی حرمت پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ دوسرا سبب یہ ہے کہ گدھے کے جھوٹے کے پاک اور ناپاک ہونے میں صحابہ کا اختلاف ہے، حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ عنہ سے اس کا ناپاک ہونا منقول ہے اور حضرت عبد اللہ بن عباس رضی اللہ عنہ سے اس کا پاک ہونا مروی ہے۔ تو ادلہ اور صحابہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے اس میں شک آگیا ، اس لئے فقہی کتب میں سور الحمار والبغل مشکوک“ کے الفاظ آئے ہیں ۔ السنن الكبرى للنسائى كتاب الوليمة، تحريم لحوم الخيل، ج ۶ ص ۲۲۳ ، رقم الحديث: ۶۶۰۶، ط: مؤسسة الرسالة] العناية: كتاب الطهارة، فصل فى الآسار، ج ا ص ۱۱۵، ط: دار الفكر / البناية: كتاب الطهارة، فصل في الآسار، ج ۱ ص ۴۹۱، ۴۹۲، ط: دار الكتب العلمية وَالْحِمَارُ وَالْبَغْلُ مَشْكُوكٌ أَى سُؤْرُهُمَا مَشْكُوكٌ فِيهِ أَمَّا الْحِمَارُ فَلِتَعَارُضِ الْأَدِلَّةِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ ثَبَتَ عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّهُ أَمَرَ يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ بِإِكْفَاءِ الْقُدُورِ مِنْ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ وَقَالَ إِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ وَرُوِيَ عَنْهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ أَنَّهُ قَالَ لِلأَبْجَرَ بُنِ غَالِبٍ حِينَ قَالَ لَهُ لَيْسَ لِي إِلَّا حَمِيرَاتٌ كُلْ مِنْ سَمِينٍ مَالِكِ وَكَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ الْكَلْبَ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَالْهِرَّةَ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَقِيلَ فِي طَهُورِيَّتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ يُشْبِهُ الْهِرَّةَ مِنْ الْوَجْهِ الَّذِى ذَكَرُنَا فَيَكُونُ طَهُورًا بِاعْتِبَارِهِ، وَيُفَارِقُهَا مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ لَا يَدْخُلُ الْمَضَايِقَ وَلَا يَصْعَدُ الْعُرَفَ فَكَانَ الْبَلْوَى فِيهِ دُونَهَا فِي الْهِرَّةِ فَيَخْرُجُ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ طَهُورًا بِاعْتِبَارِهِ فَأَوْجَبَ الشَّكَّ فِى الطَّهُورِيَّةِ وَقِيلَ الشَّكُ فِي الطَّهَارَةِ وَالطَّهُورِيَّةِ جَمِيعًا، وَأَمَّا الْبَغْلُ فَهُوَ مِنْ نَسلِ الْحِمَارِ فَيَكُونُ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ هَكَذَا. تبيين الحقائق كتاب الطهارة ، ج ا ص ۳۲، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي]
He forbade eating the flesh of horses, mules, donkeys, and every beast of prey with fangs. This hadith indicates the prohibition of donkey meat. The second reason is that there is disagreement among the Companions regarding the purity and impurity of the donkey's leftover water. It is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that it is impure, and from Abdullah ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that it is pure. Due to conflicting evidence and disagreement of the Companions, doubt arose, hence in fiqh books the phrase 'su'r of donkey and mule is doubtful' appears. The donkey and mule are doubtful, meaning their leftover water is doubtful. As for the donkey, it is due to conflicting evidence: it is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that on the day of Khaybar he ordered the overturning of cooking pots containing the meat of domestic donkeys and said 'It is impure.' And it is narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he said to Al-Abjar ibn Ghalib when he said 'I have nothing but donkeys,' 'Eat from the fat of your property.' Ibn Abbas used to say, 'Everything that feeds on grass and straw, its leftover water is pure.' And Ibn Umar used to say, 'It is impure.' And because it resembles the dog in that its meat is not eaten, and resembles the cat in that it is tied in houses and courtyards. Thus the evidence conflicted regarding it, so doubt occurred. Then some said the doubt is in its purity, for the reason we mentioned that it resembles the dog in one aspect and the cat in another. And some said the doubt is in its purifying quality, because it resembles the cat in the aspect we mentioned, so it would be purifying by that consideration, but it differs from it in that it does not enter narrow places nor climb roofs, so the affliction due to it is less than that of the cat, so it ceases to be purifying by that consideration, thus causing doubt in its purifying quality. And some said the doubt is in both purity and purifying quality. As for the mule, it is from the progeny of the donkey, so it is in its same position.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining why the su'r (leftover water) of donkeys and mules is considered mashkuk (doubtful) in the Hanafi school. The text begins by stating that both the donkey and mule are mashkuk, meaning their leftover water is doubtful in terms of purity (tahara) and purifying capability (tahuriyya). The reasoning is given step by step. First, for the donkey: there is conflicting primary evidence. On one hand, the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the overturning of pots with donkey meat at Khaybar, calling it 'rijs' (impure), which suggests najaasa. On the other hand, there is a hadith where he permitted a man to eat from his donkeys, implying they are not impure. Additionally, the Companions differed: Ibn Abbas considered the su'r of any herbivore pure, while Ibn Umar considered it impure. The text then presents an analogical reasoning (qiyas): the donkey resembles a dog in that its meat is not eaten (so su'r could be impure like a dog's) and resembles a cat in that it is kept in homes (so su'r could be pure like a cat's). Due to these conflicting analogies, doubt arises. Some scholars said the doubt is only in tahara (purity), some said in tahuriyya (purifying quality), and some said in both. The passage concludes that the mule, being the offspring of a donkey, follows the same ruling. The Hanafi position is that the su'r of these animals is not definitively pure or impure; it is mashkuk, meaning it is treated as makruh to use for wudu, and one should avoid it if possible. The authority weight is from the zahir al-riwayah, as this is a standard Hanafi ruling found in works like Tabyin al-Haqa'iq.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water that an animal drinks from; its ruling depends on the animal's status.
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; not definitively classified as pure or impure, nor as purifying or not.
طهور (tahur): Water that is itself pure and can purify other things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the su'r of the donkey considered mashkuk (doubtful) in the Hanafi school?
A) Because there is a clear hadith declaring it najis.
B) Because there is a clear hadith declaring it pure.
C) Because the evidence from hadith and Companions conflicts, and the donkey resembles both dog and cat.
D) Because the donkey is not a domestic animal.

Key Takeaway
The su'r of donkey and mule is mashkuk (doubtful) due to conflicting primary and analogical evidence, and is thus avoided for wudu when possible.
