The Hanafi Principle of Ziyada and Wudu with Nabidh
Intra-Hanafi dispute resolved by a usul principle of ziyada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that a mashhur hadith practiced by Companions can add to the Quran, and apply it to the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf over wudu with nabidh.

Core Idea
A mashhur hadith practiced by Companions can specify the Quran — but only if not retracted by the issuing Imam.

This passage from Al-Hidayah introduces a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: a hadith that is mashhur (widely known, though not mutawatir) and acted upon by the Companions can be used to 'add' (ziyada) to the Quranic text. This does not mean abrogating the Quran, but rather specifying or adding a condition not explicitly stated. The principle is then applied to an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the permissibility of performing wudu with nabidh (date infusion) when water is unavailable. Understanding this principle is crucial for seeing how the Hanafi school derives rulings from both Quran and Sunnah, and how differences within the school are resolved.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi usul principle
Identify the principle as presented in the text: a mashhur hadith that the Companions acted upon can be used to add a ruling to the Quran (ziyada 'ala al-kitab). Note that 'add' here means specify (takhsis) or provide a condition, not abrogate.
This principle is distinct from naskh (abrogation). The hadith does not override the Quran but operates alongside it.
2
Identify the dispute and its two positions
State the specific fiqh issue: wudu with nabidh when water is absent. Two Hanafi positions: Abu Hanifa permits it; Abu Yusuf prohibits it (requires tayammum).
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (both imams are within the same school).
3
Follow the proofs for each side
Abu Hanifa's evidence: the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn (Prophet performed wudu with nabidh and called it 'purifying water'). Abu Yusuf's evidence: the tayammum verse (Quran 5:6) which specifies pure earth when no water is found; he considers the hadith abrogated.
The hadith is ahad in transmission but mashhur in fame, and Companions acted on it.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response via the principle
The Hidayah argues that the hadith is not abrogated because it is mashhur and Companions acted upon it. Therefore, according to the principle, it can specify the verse and allow nabidh as a valid water substitute for wudu.
The principle is used to defend Abu Hanifa's position against the claim of abrogation.
5
Note the retraction and the mufta bihi
The passage ends with a crucial note: Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted his position. The operative fatwa (mufta bihi) now follows Abu Yusuf: wudu with nabidh is not permissible; one must perform tayammum.
This shows that later development and tarjih can override even an Imam's own earlier view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۸) إِنَّ الْحَدِيث إِذَا كَانَ مَشْهُورًا وَعَمِلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ يَصِحُ بِهِ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ . ترجمہ: جب کوئی حدیث مشہور ہو اور اس پر صحابہ کرام نے عمل کیا ہو تو ایسی مشہور حدیث سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرنا جائز ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ سے امام صاحب کے مسلک کو ثابت کیا ہے، نیز یہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کی دلیل کا جواب بھی ہے۔ مسئلہ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر نبیذ تمر کے علاوہ کوئی پانی موجود نہ ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک نبیذ تمر سے وضو کرنا جائز ہے اور تیتیم نہ کیا جائے ، جس کی دلیل حدیث لیلۃ الجن ہے،جس میں حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ فرماتے ہیں کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے نبیذ تمر سے وضو کیا اور فرمایا تمرَةٌ طَيِّبَةٌ وَمَاءً طَهُورٌ “ اس کے برخلاف امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک نبیز تمر سے وضو کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث لیلتہ الجن آیت تیم سے منسوخ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث لیلتہ الجن آیت تیم سے منسوخ نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ حدیث لیلتہ الجن مشہور ہے اور صحابہ کرام کی جماعت کا اس پر عمل بھی رہا ہے اور اصول ہے کہ جوحدیث مشہور ہو اور اس پر صحابہ نے عمل بھی کیا ہو تو ایسی مشہور حدیث سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرنا جائز ہے ،لہذا یہاں پر چونکہ یہ حدیث مشہور بھی ہے اور صحابہ کی ایک جماعت کا عمل بھی رہا ہے تو اب آیت تیم پر حدیث سے زیادتی جائز ہے، لہذا نبیذ تمر سے وضو کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اس اصول کی زیادہ واضح مثال مطلقہ ثلاثہ کی ہے، یہ شوہر اول کے لئے اس وقت تک حلال نہیں ہوگی جب تک کہ شوہر ثانی اس کے ساتھ خلوت صحیحہ یا جماع نہ کرے، یہ قید احادیث مشہورہ سے ثابت ہے جو کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی ہے۔ نوٹ: امام ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کا اس مسئلہ میں رجوع ثابت ہے، فتوی امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے مطابق ہے۔ الهداية: كتاب الطهارات، فصل فى الآسار، ص ۴۷، ط: رحمانیه
(38) Indeed, when a hadith is mashhur (famous) and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to make an increase upon the Book (Quran) through it. Translation: When a hadith is famous and the Companions acted upon it, it is permissible to add to the Book of Allah through such a mashhur hadith. Explanation: The author of Hidayah established Imam Abu Hanifa's position through the mentioned principle, and it is also a response to the evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). The gist of the issue is that if there is no water other than nabidh al-tamr (date infusion), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) it is permissible to perform wudu with nabidh al-tamr, and tayammum is not performed. Its evidence is the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn, in which Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) says that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wudu with nabidh al-tamr and said: 'A good date and purifying water.' In contrast, according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), it is not permissible to perform wudu with nabidh al-tamr; he says that the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn is abrogated by the verse of tayammum. The author of Hidayah says that the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn is not abrogated by the verse of tayammum, because the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn is mashhur and a group of Companions continued to act upon it, and the principle is that a hadith which is mashhur and the Companions acted upon it, it is permissible to add to the Book of Allah through such a mashhur hadith. Therefore, since this hadith is both mashhur and a group of Companions acted upon it, the increase upon the verse of tayammum through the hadith is permissible, so wudu with nabidh al-tamr will be permissible. A clearer example of this principle is the case of a woman divorced three times: she is not lawful for the first husband until the second husband has valid seclusion (khalwa) or intercourse with her. This condition is established through mashhur hadiths, which are an increase upon the Book of Allah. Note: It is established that Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) retracted from this ruling, and the fatwa is according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him).
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul (principle) from the Hidayah: a mashhur hadith (one known to many) that the Companions acted upon can be used to 'add' to the Quran. This does not mean abrogation (naskh) but rather specification (takhsis) or adding a condition not explicitly in the Quran. The author applies this to the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf over wudu with nabidh dates. Abu Hanifa allowed it based on the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn, while Abu Yusuf considered the hadith abrogated by the tayammum verse (Quran 5:6). The Hidayah argues that the hadith is not abrogated because it is mashhur and the Companions practiced it; thus it can specify the verse and allow wudu with nabidh when water is absent. The passage also gives another example: the condition for a thrice-divorced woman to be halal for her first husband after marrying someone else, which is a hadith-based addition to the Quran (which only mentions remarriage in principle). The note at the end clarifies that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted his position, and the fatwa now follows Abu Yusuf. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf) resolved by the later position. The authority weight of the principle itself is from the Hanafi school's usul, and the application is from the Hidayah.

Key Terms
مشهور (mashhur): A hadith known to many, but not as widely as mutawatir; it is a category between mutawatir and ahad.
زیادت علی الکتاب (ziyada 'ala al-kitab): Adding a legal rule or condition that is not explicitly in the Quran, based on a sunnah that has the strength of being mashhur and practiced.
نبیذ تمر (nabidh tamr): An infusion of dates in water, which if not left too long is not intoxicating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the verse of tayammum was revealed before the hadith.
D) Because the hadith is about a different act of worship.

Key Takeaway
A mashhur hadith with Companion practice can specify the Quran (ziyada), but its application may be overridden by an Imam's retraction or later tarjih.

Mashhur Hadith and Ziyada ala al-Kitab: The Case of Wudu with Nabidh Tamr
Usul principle with fiqh application to nabidh tamr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a mashhur hadith acted upon by Companions can add to the Quranic ruling, and apply it to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu with nabidh tamr and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A mashhur hadith with Companion practice can supplement the Quran; this principle resolves the dispute on wudu with nabidh tamr.

This lesson explores a foundational Hanafi usul principle: when a hadith is well-known (mashhur) and the Companions acted upon it, it can add a ruling not explicitly in the Quran. We'll see how this principle is deployed in the famous disagreement over wudu with date infusion (nabidh tamr) when no pure water exists, and why the final operative ruling requires tayammum instead.

Guided Path
1
State the usul principle
Read the first sentence: 'When a hadith is mashhur and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to increase upon the Book by it.' This is the core rule.
The principle only applies to mashhur hadith, not ahad.
2
Understand the authority of mashhur hadith
A mashhur hadith is transmitted by at least three companions in each generation, giving it a level of certainty higher than ahad but still zanni al-thubut. Companion practice confirms its acceptance.
Hanafis consider mashhur as nearly certain in meaning when companions apply it.
3
Apply to the wudu dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa used the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn to permit wudu with nabidh tamr. Imam Abu Yusuf argued it is abrogated by the tayammum verse. The author of Al-Hidayah responds that the hadith is mashhur and practiced, so it adds to the verse—not abrogate it.
This is a key example of using the principle to defend a ruling against naskh.
4
Recognize the ruju' and final fatwa
Despite the principle, Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted his view. The mufta bihi is that tayammum is wajib and wudu with nabidh tamr is invalid.
The ruju' is reported in later sources; fatwa follows Abu Yusuf and the three Imams.
5
Connect to another example
The passage also mentions the thrice-divorced woman: a mashhur hadith adds the condition of consummation by a second husband, which is not in the Quran.
This illustrates the principle's broader application.

(وبمثله) أى بمثل هذا الحديث يزاد على الكتاب وتمسكه أى وتمسك هذا الحديث مبنى على الكتاب كما فى المطلقة ثلاثا فإنه يراد الدخول عليه بالحديث المشهور.

(38) Indeed, when a hadith is mashhur (widely transmitted) and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to increase upon the Book by it. Translation: When a hadith is mashhur and the noble Companions acted upon it, then by such a mashhur hadith, increasing upon the Book of Allah is permissible. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah has proven the position of Imam Abu Hanifa through this mentioned principle, and it is also a response to the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf. The summary of the issue is that if there is no water other than nabidh tamr (date infusion), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, performing wudu with nabidh tamr is permissible and tayammum is not required; its proof is the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn, in which Abdullah ibn Mas'ud says that the Prophet performed wudu with nabidh tamr and said: 'A good date and purifying water.' In contrast, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, wudu with nabidh tamr is not permissible; he says that the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn is abrogated by the verse of tayammum. The author of al-Hidayah says that the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn is not abrogated by the verse of tayammum, because the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn is mashhur and a group of Companions acted upon it, and the principle is that whichever hadith is mashhur and the Companions acted upon it, then increasing upon the Book of Allah by such a mashhur hadith is permissible. Therefore, since this hadith is both mashhur and acted upon by a group of Companions, increasing upon the verse of tayammum by the hadith is permissible, so wudu with nabidh tamr is permissible. A clearer example of this principle is the thrice-divorced woman; she is not lawful for the first husband until the second husband has valid seclusion or intercourse with her—this condition is proven by mashhur ahadith, which is an increase upon the Book of Allah. Note: The return (ruju') of Imam Abu Hanifa in this issue is established; the fatwa is upon the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf and the three Imams that wudu with nabidh tamr is not permissible; rather tayammum is necessary. (And by the like of it) meaning by the like of this hadith, it is increased upon the Book, and its holding fast means holding fast to this hadith is based on the Book, as in the case of the thrice-divorced woman, for entering upon her is intended by the mashhur hadith. Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi usul principle and its application to a fiqh ruling. The principle is that a mashhur (well-known) hadith that was acted upon by the Companions can add an obligation or condition to the Quranic text. This is used to refute the claim of abrogation made by Imam Abu Yusuf regarding wudu with nabidh tamr. The text explains the dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa initially permitted wudu with date infusion when no pure water is available, citing the hadith of Laylat al-Jinn; Imam Abu Yusuf held that this hadith is abrogated by the tayammum verse. Al-Hidayah argues that the hadith is mashhur and companions practiced it, so it can supplement the Quran, making wudu valid. However, a note clarifies that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted, and the fatwa is now on the view of Abu Yusuf and the three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) that tayammum is required. The passage also gives an example of the thrice-divorced woman, where a mashhur hadith adds the condition of consummation by a second husband, which is not explicit in the Quran.

Key Terms
مشہور (mashhūr): A hadith transmitted by at least three companions in each generation, but not reaching mutawatir; it is stronger than ahad but still zanni al-thubut.
زیادہ علی الکتاب (ziyāda 'alā al-kitāb): Adding a ruling not explicitly found in the Quran through a mashhur hadith with Companion practice.
نبیذ تمر (nabīdh tamr): A drink made by soaking dates in water, used for wudu in the absence of pure water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in this passage, when can a hadith add an obligation to the Quran?
A) When the hadith is mashhur and the Companions acted upon it.
B) When the hadith is mutawatir.
C) When the hadith is ahad.
D) When the hadith is agreed upon by all mujtahids.

Key Takeaway
A mashhur hadith with Companion practice can supplement the Quran without abrogating it, but the final Hanafi fatwa on wudu with nabidh tamr requires tayammum due to Abu Hanifa's ruju'.

The Principle of Real Inability for Tayammum
Ruling principle with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that real inability (ʿajz haqiqi) makes tayammum wajib and apply it to scenarios involving fear of harm from water.

Core Idea
Real inability to use water makes tayammum obligatory – rational necessity.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi principle in taharah: when a person truly cannot use water due to genuine fear of death or illness, the obligation shifts from wudu/gusl to tayammum. The principle is proven by rational proof (dalil aqli) and is agreed upon within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the act as tayammum in place of wudu/gusl when unable to use water. The ruling is that tayammum becomes wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the rational principle: 'When inability is established in reality, it must be considered.' (إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اِعْتِبَارِهِ).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The obligation of wudu is conditional on ability. If using water causes genuine harm (death/illness), the person is effectively unable, so wudu is not required, and tayammum becomes the substitute.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This principle is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) within the Hanafi school and with other schools.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that tayammum is obligatory when real fear of harm exists, as confirmed by Tahawi and later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۹) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اِعْتِبَارِهِ.
ترجمہ: جب عجز حقیقتاً ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ کو بطور دلیل عقلی کے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر جنبی آدمی کو یہ خوف ہو کہ غسل کرنے کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہو جائے گا یا بیمار ہو جائے گا تو اس کے واسطے تیم کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ جنبی ایسی حالت میں غسل کرنے سے حقیقتا عاجز ہے اور اس کا بجز درحقیقت ثابت ہے
(قَوْلُهُ وَيُقَدِّمُ التَّيَمُّمَ عَلَى نَبِيدِ الشَّمْسِ إِعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ رُوِيَ فِى النَّبِيدِ عَنْ الْإِمَامِ ثَلَاتُ رِوَايَاتِ : الْأُولَى وَهِيَ قَوْلُهُ الْأَوَّلُ أَنَّهُ يَتَوَضَّأُ بِهِ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يُضِيفَ إِلَيْهِ التَّيَمُّمَ الثَّانِيَةُ: اَلْجَمْعُ بَيْنَهُمَا كَسُؤُرِ الْحِمَارِ، وَبِهِ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ وَرَبَّحَهُ فِي غَايَةِ الْبَيَانِ وَالثَّالِثَةُ: التَّيَمُّمُ فَقَط، وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ الْأَخِيرُ، وَقَدْ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ، وَبِهِ قَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَالْأَئِمَّةُ الثَّلَاثَةُ وَاخْتَارَهُ الطَّحَاوِيُّ، وَهُوَ الْمَذْهَبُ الْمُصَرَّحُ الْمُخْتَارُ الْمُعْتَمَدُ عِنْدَنَا بَحْرٌ.
ردالمختار كتاب الطهارة، باب المياه، فصل في البئر، ج ۱ ص ۲۲۷، ط: دار الفكر
وَرَوَى أَسَدُ بْنُ نَجْمِ وَنُوحُ بْنُ أَبِي مَرْيَمَ وَالْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ رَجَعَ إِلَى قَوْلِ أَبِى يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ وَالصَّحِيحُ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ الْآخَرُ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ. كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ لِلْإِمَامِ قَاضِي خَانُ وَالْفَتْوَى عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ كَذَا فِي الْعَيْنِي شَرح الْكَنُرِ.
الفتاوى الهندية كتاب الطهارة، الباب الثالث الفصل الثاني ج ۱ ص ۲۲، ط: دار الفکر]
الهداية: كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۴۹، ط: رحمانیه
(39) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, then it must be considered. Translation: When inability is truly established, then considering it is necessary. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah has mentioned this principle as a rational proof that if a person in a state of janabah fears that due to washing he will die or become ill, then tayammum is permissible for him, because in such a state he is truly unable to perform washing, and his inability is established in reality. (His statement: And he gives precedence to tayammum over nabidh al-shams. Know that regarding nabidh, three narrations are reported from the Imam: the first is his first statement that one performs wudu with it and it is recommended to add tayammum to it; the second is to combine between them like the leftover of a donkey, and Muhammad said this and he preferred it in Ghayat al-Bayan; and the third is tayammum only, and that is his final statement, and he retracted to it, and Abu Yusuf and the three Imams said it, and al-Tahawi chose it, and it is the explicit, chosen, relied-upon madhhab with us. Radd al-Muhtar: Book of Taharah, Chapter on Waters, Section on the Well, vol. 1, p. 227, Dar al-Fikr. And Asad ibn Najm, Nuh ibn Abi Maryam, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he retracted to the statement of Abu Yusuf, and the correct is the other statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. So in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Qadi Khan, and the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf, so in al-Ayni's Sharh al-Kanz. Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah: Book of Taharah, Chapter Three, Section Two, vol. 1, p. 22, Dar al-Fikr. Al-Hidayah: Book of Taharah, Chapter on Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 49, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi principle regarding considering real inability for tayammum. The principle is that when a person is truly unable to use water due to genuine fear of death or illness, tayammum becomes obligatory. The text explains this as a rational proof: since the person cannot perform wudu without harm, they are effectively unable, so the obligation shifts to tayammum. The additional quotes from Radd al-Muhtar and Fatawa Hindiyyah provide further evidence from the Hanafi school, confirming that Imam Abu Hanifa eventually retracted his earlier views on nabidh tamr and that the final madhhab is tayammum only, in agreement with Abu Yusuf and the three Imams.

Key Terms
عجز (ʿajz): Inability or incapacity to perform an act, here specifically inability to use water for wudu due to genuine fear of harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When the person fears genuine harm from using water.
C) When water is too cold.
D) When traveling.

Key Takeaway
Real inability to use water due to genuine harm triggers the obligation of tayammum.

The Hanafi Ruling on Nabidh al-Shams and Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nabidh for wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on using nabidh for wudu and identify the final mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa eventually retracted to the position that only tayammum is used, in agreement with Abu Yusuf and the majority.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding nabidh al-shams (date water left in the sun). While the focus of the chapter is tayammum, the passage includes a key ikhtilaf: can one use nabidh for wudu? The lesson traces the three narrations from Abu Hanifa and the final reliance on tayammum only.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether nabidh al-shams (date water) can be used for wudu or whether tayammum alone suffices.
2
List the three narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa
First narration: perform wudu with nabidh and recommend adding tayammum. Second: combine both (like the leftover of a donkey). Third: tayammum only (final position retracted to).
3
Note the positions of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf agreed with the third (tayammum only). Muhammad agreed with the second (combine).
4
Identify the chosen position
Al-Tahawi and later scholars chose the third (tayammum only), and it is the explicit, relied-upon madhhab.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that tayammum only is required; wudu with nabidh is not valid.

The Principle of Real Inability and Its Application to Tayammum
States the legal principle of real inability and applies it to tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of real inability and apply it to determine when tayammum is wajib.

Core Idea
Real inability to use water makes tayammum wajib — the incapacity is legally recognized.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh: when a person is truly unable to use water due to fear of death or illness, the Sharia recognizes that inability and permits tayammum instead. The author of Al-Hidayah presents this as a rational proof (dalil 'aqli). We will examine how this principle operates in the case of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The passage states: 'Indeed, when inability is established in reality, it must be considered.' This is the core legal maxim governing tayammum.
The principle is presented as a general rule in Chapter of Tayammum.
2
Recognize the type of proof
The author calls this a 'dalil 'aqli' (rational proof). It is not derived from a specific text but from the general objectives of Sharia to remove hardship.
Hanafi usul recognizes rational proofs as valid when based on clear reasoning.
3
Apply to the junub case
If a junub person fears that using water for ghusl will cause death or illness, his inability is real. Therefore, the principle applies, and tayammum becomes wajib.
This applies regardless of location (city or village).
4
Note the scope and condition
The condition is 'real inability' (al-'ajz al-haqiqi), not mere inconvenience. The fear must be substantiated by experience or medical advice.
This differentiates from cases where water is simply cold but not harmful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے قول پر ہے کہ نبیذ تمر سے وضو جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ تیم ضروری ہے۔
باب التيمم
(۳۹) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اِعْتِبَارِهِ.
ترجمہ: جب عجز حقیقتاً ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ کو بطور دلیل عقلی کے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر جنبی آدمی کو یہ خوف ہو کہ غسل کرنے کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہو جائے گا یا بیمار ہو جائے گا تو اس کے واسطے تیم کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ جنبی ایسی حالت میں غسل کرنے سے حقیقتا عاجز ہے اور اس کا بجز درحقیقت ثابت ہے
(وبمثله) أى بمثل هذا الحديث يزاد على الكتاب وتمسكه أى وتمسك هذا الحديث
مبنى على الكتاب كما فى المطلقة ثلاثا فإنه يراد الدخول عليه بالحديث المشهور.
البناية كتاب الطهارة، فصل في الآسار، ج ۱ ص ۵۰۶، ط: دار الكتب العلمية] (قَوْلُهُ وَيُقَدِّمُ التَّيَمُّمَ عَلَى نَبِيدِ الشَّمْسِ إِعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ رُوِيَ فِى النَّبِيدِ عَنْ الْإِمَامِ ثَلَاتُ رِوَايَاتِ : الْأُولَى وَهِيَ قَوْلُهُ الْأَوَّلُ أَنَّهُ يَتَوَضَّأُ بِهِ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يُضِيفَ إِلَيْهِ التَّيَمُّمَ الثَّانِيَةُ: اَلْجَمْعُ بَيْنَهُمَا كَسُؤُرِ الْحِمَارِ، وَبِهِ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ وَرَبَّحَهُ فِي غَايَةِ الْبَيَانِ وَالثَّالِثَةُ: التَّيَمُّمُ فَقَط، وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ الْأَخِيرُ، وَقَدْ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ، وَبِهِ قَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَالْأَئِمَّةُ الثَّلَاثَةُ وَاخْتَارَهُ الطَّحَاوِيُّ، وَهُوَ الْمَذْهَبُ الْمُصَرَّحُ الْمُخْتَارُ الْمُعْتَمَدُ عِنْدَنَا بَحْرٌ.
ردالمختار كتاب الطهارة، باب المياه، فصل في البئر، ج ۱ ص ۲۲۷، ط: دار الفكر وَرَوَى أَسَدُ بْنُ نَجْمِ وَنُوحُ بْنُ أَبِي مَرْيَمَ وَالْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ رَجَعَ إِلَى قَوْلِ أَبِى يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ وَالصَّحِيحُ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ الْآخَرُ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ. كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ لِلْإِمَامِ قَاضِي خَانُ وَالْفَتْوَى عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ كَذَا فِي الْعَيْنِي شَرح الْكَنُرِ.
الفتاوى الهندية كتاب الطهارة، الباب الثالث الفصل الثاني ج ۱ ص ۲۲، ط: دار الفکر] الهداية: كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۴۹، ط: رحمانیه

چاہے وہ شہر میں ہو یا دیہات میں ہو، علت بجز ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ جب بجز حقیقتاً ثابت ہو تو اس کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہے، تو یہاں پر بھی چونکہ جنبی کے لئے بجز ثابت ہے لہذا اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور اس کے لئے تیتم کرنا جائز ہوگا۔
And it is according to the statement of the three Imams that wudu with date nabidh is not permissible, rather tayammum is necessary. Chapter of Tayammum. (39) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, it must be considered. Translation: When inability is truly established, it is necessary to take it into account. Explanation: The author of Hidayah mentioned this principle as an intellectual proof: if a junub person fears that due to performing ghusl he will die or become ill, then tayammum for him is permissible, because the junub in such a state is truly unable to perform ghusl, and his inability is established in reality. (And by similar) i.e., by a hadith like this, addition is made to the Book, and its retention is based on the Book, as in the case of a threefold divorce where entry (marriage) is desired based on the famous hadith. Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Tahara, Fasl fi al-Asar, vol. 1 p. 506, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya. (His statement: And he gives precedence to tayammum over nabidh made from dates. Know that concerning nabidh, three narrations are reported from the Imam: the first, which is his first opinion, that one performs wudu with it and it is recommended to add tayammum to it; the second: combining both like the leftover of a donkey, and Muhammad held this and authenticated it in Ghayat al-Bayan; the third: tayammum only, and this is his final opinion, and he retracted (from the first) to it, and Abu Yusuf and the three Imams held this, and al-Tahawi chose it, and it is the clearly chosen relied-upon madhhab with us. Radd al-Muhtar: Kitab al-Tahara, Bab al-Miyah, Fasl fi al-Bi'r, vol. 1 p. 227, Dar al-Fikr. And Asad ibn Najm, Nuh ibn Abi Maryam, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he retracted to the statement of Abu Yusuf, and the correct is the other statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Thus in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Qadi Khan, and the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf, thus in al-'Ayni's Sharh al-Kanz. Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya: Kitab al-Tahara, al-Bab al-Thalith, al-Fasl al-Thani, vol. 1 p. 22, Dar al-Fikr. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Taharat, Bab al-Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 49, Rahmaniyya. Whether he (the junub) is in the city or the village, the cause is inability, and the principle is that when inability is truly established, it is necessary to consider it. So here too, since inability is established for the junub, it will be considered, and tayammum for him will be permissible.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental Hanafi usul al-fiqh principle: real inability (al-'ajz al-haqiqi) must be legally recognized. The author of Hidayah cites it as a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) for permitting tayammum when using water would cause death or illness. The principle is then applied to two cases. First, the case of a junub (person in major impurity) who fears harm from cold water: tayammum is allowed even in a city, because the inability is real. Second, the passage discusses the ruling on using nabidh (date-water) for wudu. Imam Abu Hanifa initially allowed wudu with nabidh (with recommended tayammum), then allowed combining both, and finally retracted to the position of tayammum only. This final position is agreed upon by Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad), making it the relied-upon (mu'tamad) view in the Hanafi school. The passage emphasizes that the principle of real inability overrides other considerations, even in rare situations.

Key Terms
عجز (ajz): Inability to use water due to genuine fear of harm (death or illness).
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A junub person is in a cold climate and fears that using cold water for ghusl will cause pneumonia. According to the principle in this lesson, what should he do?
A) He must perform ghusl with cold water regardless.
B) He may perform tayammum instead of ghusl.
C) He should use warm water if available, otherwise tayammum is not allowed.
D) He must perform tayammum and then ghusl when he warms up.

Key Takeaway
Real inability to use water due to harm makes tayammum wajib, and this principle overrides the general obligation to use water.

The Ruling on Wudu with Nabidh (Date-Water): The Three Narrations and the Mufta Bihi
Discusses the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on wudu with nabidh and settles on the final position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding wudu with nabidh and state the final relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Using nabidh for wudu is invalid; the final Hanafi position is tayammum only when pure water is unavailable.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether date-water (nabidh) can be used for wudu when pure water is unavailable. Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have three opinions. We will trace these narrations, see how the principle of real inability applies, and identify the mufta bihi ruling that settles the issue.

Guided Path
1
List the three narrations from Abu Hanifa
First: wudu with nabidh and recommended tayammum. Second: combine both (like leftover of donkey). Third: tayammum only.
These narrations reflect an evolution in Abu Hanifa's ijtihad.
2
Identify the final position
Abu Hanifa retracted to the third narration (tayammum only). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad also supported this. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
The retraction is narrated by Asad ibn Najm, Nuh ibn Abi Maryam, and al-Hasan.
3
Note the authority
The third narration is chosen by al-Tahawi, and endorsed by later authorities like Al-Hidayah, Radd al-Muhtar, and Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah.
Thus, the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf and the final view of Abu Hanifa.
4
Apply the principle of real inability
If pure water is not available, the inability to obtain it is real. Nabidh is not water, so it does not remove the inability. Therefore tayammum is wajib.
This shows the consistent application of the principle from lesson 1.
5
State the practical ruling
A traveler who has only nabidh must perform tayammum; wudu with nabidh is invalid and does not fulfill the obligation of taharah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

باب التيمم
(۳۹) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اِعْتِبَارِهِ.
ترجمہ: جب عجز حقیقتاً ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ کو بطور دلیل عقلی کے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر جنبی آدمی کو یہ خوف ہو کہ غسل کرنے کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہو جائے گا یا بیمار ہو جائے گا تو اس کے واسطے تیم کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ جنبی ایسی حالت میں غسل کرنے سے حقیقتا عاجز ہے اور اس کا بجز درحقیقت ثابت ہے
(وبمثله) أى بمثل هذا الحديث يزاد على الكتاب وتمسكه أى وتمسك هذا الحديث

According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should a traveler do if he only has nabidh (date-water) available?
A) Perform wudu with nabidh and it is valid.
B) Perform wudu with nabidh and add tayammum as recommended.

Sleeping Person Legally Capable of Water
States that a sleeping person is deemed capable of water by legal estimation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sleeping person is legally capable of water and apply it to determine the validity of tayammum.

Core Idea
A sleeping person is legally considered capable of water because his inability is due to his own shortcoming.

This lesson explains a key Hanafi principle in tayammum: the status of a sleeping person who becomes able to use water. According to Abu Hanifa, the sleeping person is not excused; his tayammum becomes invalid if he passes water, even while asleep. The reasoning is based on the distinction between real inability and self-caused inability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is tayammum performed by a sleeping person who later becomes able to use water. The ruling: the tayammum becomes invalid.
2
Understand 'qadir taqdiran'
This term means 'legally capable by estimation'. It is a legal construct, not physical capability. The sleeping person is treated as capable because the inability stems from his own sleep.
3
Distinguish real vs. self-caused inability
The passage contrasts the sleeping person (self-caused) with a junub in the city fearing cold (real inability). In the latter, tayammum remains valid until the fear passes.
4
Apply to the resident scenario
The example: a resident (muqim) sleeping passes water; his tayammum becomes invalid. This applies even if he is unaware.
5
Note authority and cross-madhhab difference
This is Abu Hanifa's view, supported by later Hanafi authorities. Other schools might consider the sleeping person excused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۰) إِنَّ النَّائِمَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ . .
ترجمہ: بحالت تیم سویا ہوا شخص حکما پانی پر قادر شمار ہوگا۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ کا مقصود اس اصول سے یہ ہے کہ سویا ہوا شخص بھی پانی پر قادر شمار ہوگا، چنانچہ اگر کوئی مقیم سونے کی حالت میں پانی سے گزرا تو اس کا تیم باطل ہو جائے گا، اس لئے کہ یہ حکماً پانی پر قادر ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص پانی کے استعمال سے ایسے عذر ( نیند ) کی وجہ سے عاجز ہوا جو خود اس کی جانب سے پیدا ہوا ہے، لہذا اس کو معذور نہیں سمجھا جائے گا، اس کا تیم باطل ہو جائے گا۔ (أَوُ الْجُنُبُ فِي الْمِصْرِ) أَى تَيَمَّمَ الْجُنُّبُ فِي الْمِصْرِ لِخَوْفِ الْبَرْدِ جَازَ عِنْدَ الْإِمَامِ، لِأَنَّ الْعَجْزَ ثَابِتٌ حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ ثُمَّ إِنْ رُحْصَةَ التَّيَمُّمِ بِسَبَبِ الْبَرْدِ ثَابِتَةٌ لِلْمُحْدِثِ أَيْضًا عَلَى مَا ذَكَرَهُ السَّرَخُسِيُّ.
[مجمع الأنهر: كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ۴۴، ط: دار إحياء التراث] أن العجز ثابت حقيقة إذ الغرض خوف الهلاك مع وجود الماء ومشروعية التيمم لدفع الحرج وهو شامل لهما فلا بد من اعتباره ولو كتان نادراً في المصر إذا تحقق فلا بد أنيجب الخروج عند عهدته، ولهذا لو عدم الماء في المصر يتيمم ولو كان نادراً.
[البناية: كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ۵۱۹، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ]
الهداية كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۵۱، ط: رحمانیه
بأَنَّ النَّوْمَ فِي حَالَةِ السَّفَر عَلَى وَجْهِ لَا يَشْعُرُ بِالْمَاءِ نَادِرٌ خُصُوصًا عَلَى وَجْهِ لَا يَتَخَلَّلُهُ الْيَقِظَةُ الْمُشْعِرَةُ بِالْمَاءِ فَلَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ نَوْمُهُ فَجُعِلَ كَالْيَقْطَان حُكْمًا أَوْ لأَنَّ التَّقْصِيرَ مِنْهُ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ الَّذِي لَمْ يَعْلَمُ بِالْمَاءِ، وَهُوَ قَرِيبٌ مِنْهُ يُؤَيِّدُهُ قَوْلُ الْهِدَايَةِ وَالنَّائِمُ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ.
[ منحة الخالق كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ١ ١٦ ، ط: دار الكتاب الاسلامي]
(40) Indeed, the sleeping person is capable by estimation according to Abu Hanifa. Translation: In the state of tayammum, a sleeping person will be considered legally capable of water. Explanation: The author of Hidayah intends by this principle that a sleeping person will also be considered capable of water. Thus, if a resident passes by water while asleep, his tayammum becomes invalid, because he is legally capable of water, since this person's inability to use water is due to an excuse (sleep) that arises from his own side; therefore he will not be considered excused, and his tayammum becomes invalid. (Or the junub in the city) i.e., if a junub performs tayammum in the city due to fear of cold, it is permissible according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), because the inability is established in reality, so it must be considered. Then, indeed, the concession for tayammum due to cold is established for the one in minor impurity as well, as stated by al-Sarakhsi. [Majma' al-Anhur: Kitab al-Tahara, Bab al-Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 44, Dar Ihya' al-Turath] that the inability is real because the purpose is fear of destruction despite the presence of water, and the legislation of tayammum is to remove hardship, which includes both, so it must be considered, even if rare in the city if it occurs, then it is necessary to exit from the responsibility; hence if water is absent in the city, one performs tayammum even if rare. [Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Tahara, Bab al-Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 519, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya] Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Taharat, Bab al-Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 51, Rahmaniyya. Because sleeping in a state of travel in a manner that one does not sense water is rare, especially in a manner not interspersed with awareness that indicates water, so his sleep is not considered, and he is made like one awake legally. Or because the shortcoming is from him, unlike one who did not know of the water. And that which is close to him supports the statement of al-Hidayah: 'The sleeping person is capable by estimation according to Abu Hanifa.' [Minhat al-Khaliq: Kitab al-Tahara, Bab al-Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 116, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami]
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi legal principle: a sleeping person is legally considered capable of using water (qadir taqdiran) according to Abu Hanifa. The practical effect is that if a muqim (resident) who has performed tayammum walks past water while asleep, his tayammum becomes invalid. This is because his inability is due to his own negligence (sleep), so he is not considered excused. The same principle applies to a junub in the city who fears cold: tayammum is permissible because the inability is real. The commentary from Majma' al-Anhur and Al-Binayah emphasizes that real inability must be considered even in rare cases. The Minhat al-Khaliq explains that the sleeping person is treated like one awake because his sleep is a shortcoming from him, unlike one who genuinely does not know about the water. Thus, the ruling reinforces the idea that tayammum is invalidated when one becomes able to use water, even if unaware.

Key Terms
نائم (na'im): A person who is asleep and unaware of his surroundings, specifically in the context of passing water while in a state of tayammum.
قادر تقديرا (qadir taqdiran): Legally considered capable by estimation, even if physically unable due to own fault.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution; in this context, it is a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a resident's tayammum if he passes by water while asleep?
A) It remains valid because he is unaware.
B) It becomes invalid because he is legally capable.
C) It remains valid but he must repeat tayammum upon waking.
D) It becomes invalid only if he is travelling.

Key Takeaway
A sleeping person is legally capable of water (qadir taqdiran) according to Abu Hanifa, so tayammum becomes invalid immediately upon ability, even if unaware.

The Sleeper's Tayammum: Legally Able Despite Sleep
States the principle about the sleeping person's legal ability to use water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sleeping person's tayammum is invalid when water becomes available, and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas and istihsan) behind it.

Core Idea
A sleeper is not excused for tayammum because his inability is self-inflicted; he is legally able.

In this lesson, we unpack a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah: a sleeping person who performs tayammum and later water passes by during sleep has his tayammum invalidated. Why? Because sleep is not considered a genuine excuse—the inability is self-caused. We will explore the principle of 'qādirun taqdīran' (legally deemed able) and contrast it with a real inability like fear of cold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Ruling
The passage states that a sleeping person performing tayammum will have his tayammum invalidated if water passes by him during sleep. This is the operative ruling.
2
Understand the Key Principle
The sleeper is considered 'qādirun taqdīran' (legally able) because his inability (sleep) is a self-inflicted state. This is a constructive legal capacity used to deny the concession of tayammum.
This principle is specific to Abu Hanifa and is the relied-upon view.
3
Trace the Legal Reasoning (Dalil)
The principle is derived via qiyas: just as a person who intentionally avoids water is not excused, the sleeper who voluntarily sleeps is also not excused. Istihsan may sometimes override, but here it does not because the inability is not genuine.
The proof is rational, not from nas.
4
Note the Exception (Junub in City)
The passage contrasts with the case of a junub in the city who fears cold. That is a real inability (fear of harm), so tayammum is permissible. The difference is that the inability is not self-inflicted.
Both major and minor impurity persons can use this concession according to Sarakhsi.
5
Apply the Distinction
In practice, the sleeper's tayammum is invalid if water becomes available; the junub's tayammum remains valid as long as the fear of cold exists. This distinction hinges on the cause of inability.

Source Text

ترجمہ: بحالت تیم سویا ہوا شخص حکما پانی پر قادر شمار ہوگا۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ کا مقصود اس اصول سے یہ ہے کہ سویا ہوا شخص بھی پانی پر قادر شمار ہوگا، چنانچہ اگر کوئی مقیم سونے کی حالت میں پانی سے گزرا تو اس کا تیم باطل ہو جائے گا، اس لئے کہ یہ حکماً پانی پر قادر ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص پانی کے استعمال سے ایسے عذر ( نیند ) کی وجہ سے عاجز ہوا جو خود اس کی جانب سے پیدا ہوا ہے، لہذا اس کو معذور نہیں سمجھا جائے گا، اس کا تیم باطل ہو جائے گا۔ (أَوُ الْجُنُبُ فِي الْمِصْرِ) أَى تَيَمَّمَ الْجُنُّبُ فِي الْمِصْرِ لِخَوْفِ الْبَرْدِ جَازَ عِنْدَ الْإِمَامِ، لِأَنَّ الْعَجْزَ ثَابِتٌ حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ ثُمَّ إِنْ رُحْصَةَ التَّيَمُّمِ بِسَبَبِ الْبَرْدِ ثَابِتَةٌ لِلْمُحْدِثِ أَيْضًا عَلَى مَا ذَكَرَهُ السَّرَخُسِيُّ.

[البناية: كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ۵۱۹، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ]
الهداية كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۵۱، ط: رحمانیه

Whether it is in the city or the village, the inability is the cause, and the principle is that when the inability is actually proven, it is necessary to consider it. So here, since the inability is proven for the junub, it will be considered, and tayammum will be permissible for him. (40) Indeed, the sleeping person is legally considered able according to Abu Hanifa. Translation: In a state of tayammum, a sleeping person is legally considered able to access water. Explanation: The author of Hidayah intends by this principle that a sleeping person is also considered able to access water. Thus, if a resident passes by water while sleeping, his tayammum becomes invalid, because he is legally able to access water, as he became incapable due to an excuse (sleep) that arose from his own side. Therefore, he will not be considered excused, and his tayammum will be invalid. (Or the junub in the city) That is, if a junub in the city performs tayammum due to fear of cold, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the inability is real, so it must be considered. Then, the concession of tayammum due to cold is also established for the one with minor impurity (hadath), as mentioned by al-Sarakhsi. [Majma' al-Anhur: Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 44] That the inability is real because the purpose is fear of destruction with the presence of water, and the legislation of tayammum is to remove hardship, and it includes both, so it must be considered, even if it is rare in the city when it is confirmed, then one must exit from its responsibility. Hence, if water is absent in the city, one performs tayammum even if it is rare. [al-Binayah: Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 519] al-Hidayah, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 51: Because sleep during travel in a way that one is unaware of water is rare, especially in a way that wakefulness that indicates water does not intervene, so his sleep was not considered, and he was made like one awake legally. Or because the shortcoming is from him, and not so for the one who did not know about the water, and it is close to it. This is supported by the statement of al-Hidayah: 'And the sleeper is legally considered able according to Abu Hanifa.' [Minhat al-Khaliq, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 116]

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah and its commentaries on the topic of tayammum. It states the principle that a sleeping person is legally deemed able to access water according to Abu Hanifa, even if in reality he is asleep. This means that if a resident (muqim) falls asleep and during his sleep water passes nearby, his tayammum is invalidated because he is considered able to use water. The reasoning is that his inability (sleep) is a fault arising from his own action, so he is not excused. The passage then extends this to the case of a junub (one in major impurity) in a city who fears cold: his tayammum is permissible because the inability is real (fear of harm). The commentary clarifies that the same concession applies to those with minor impurity. Supporting texts from Majma' al-Anhur and al-Binayah emphasize that the inability must be real and that the concession for tayammum is based on removing hardship. The passage concludes by noting that sleep causing unawareness of water is rare, so the sleeper is treated like one awake.

Key Terms
نائم (nā'im): A sleeping person; legally considered able to access water if water passes by during sleep, thus invalidating tayammum.
قادر تقديرًا (qādirun taqdīran): Legally deemed able; a person is considered capable of using water even if asleep, because the inability is self-inflicted.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does a sleeping resident's tayammum become invalid if water passes by?
A) Because sleep is a valid excuse
B) Because he is legally deemed able to access water since his inability is self-inflicted
C) Because water is not available in the city
D) Because he did not have the intention to use water

Key Takeaway
A sleeping person is legally considered able to access water, so his tayammum is invalid if water becomes available; the inability must be real and not self-inflicted.

The Tool of Purification Must Be Pure
States the principle that the instrument used for purification must itself be pure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the tool of purification must be pure and explain its proof from the Quranic command of pure earth.

Core Idea
The instrument of purification must itself be pure — a condition derived from Quranic interpretation and consensus.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author establishes a fundamental principle: any medium used for purification, such as earth for tayammum or water for wudu, must itself be ritually pure (tahir). This lesson unpacks the proof from the Quran and explains why this condition is essential for the validity of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recognize the general rule: the tool of purification must be pure in itself. This applies to both water and earth.
2
Locate the proof
Find the Quranic evidence: 'sa'idan tayyiban' (pure earth) in Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6. Note that 'tayyib' is interpreted as 'tahir' by consensus.
3
Understand the condition
The condition is that the earth must be pure (free from najasah) for tayammum to be valid. This is a shart for the act.
4
Note the consensus
The four Imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree. Only Dawud al-Zahiri differed regarding earth that is not changed by impurity.
5
Apply the analogy
Just as water must be pure for wudu, earth must be pure for tayammum. This is based on the principle that the tool of purification inherits the condition of purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۱) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ طَهَارَتِهِ فِي نَفْسِهِ.
ترجمہ: جو چیز پاک کرنے کا آلہ ہو تو اس کا خود پاک ہونا بھی ضروری ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے یہ بتانا چاہتے ہیں کہ تیم جس چیز سے کیا جائے اس کا خود پاک ہونا ضروری ہے، تیم کرنے والے کے لئے مٹی پاک کرنے کا آلہ ہے، لہذا جس طرح پانی پاک کرنے کا آلہ ہے اور بذات خود پاک ہے، اسی طرح مٹی کا بھی بذات خود پاک ہونا ضروری ہے۔
وَالنَّائِمُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا وَخَائِفُ السَّبُعِ عَاجِزٌ حُكْمًا، وَالْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ النَّائِمِ وَالْخَائِفِ أَنَّ النَّوْمَ فِي حَالَةِ السَّفَرِ عَلَى وَجْهِ لَا يَشْعُرُ بِالْمَاءِ نَادِرٌ خُصُوصًا عَلَى وَجْهِ لَا يَتَخَلَّلُهُ الْيَقَظَةُ الْمُشْعِرَةُ بِالْمَاءِ فَلَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ نَوْمُهُ كَالْيَقْطَانِ حُكْمًا.
الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ۲۴، ط: المطبعة الخيرية
ص
الهداية كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۵۲، ط: رحمانیه
ولا يتيمم إلا بصعيد طاهر لأن الطيب المذكور فى قَوْله تَعَالَى: (صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا) (أريد به الطاهر في النص بالإجماع، إذ طهارة التراب شرط عند الأئمة الأربعة، وعن داود والتراب إذا تغير بالنجاسة لا يجوز التيمم به، وإن لم يتغير جاز، ويجوز التيمم بالتراب المستعمل عندنا. [ البناية: كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ۵۵۰، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ولا يجوز التيمم إلا بالصعيد الطاهر لأن الطيب أريد به الطاهر، ولأنه آلة التطهير، فلابد من طهارته فى نفسه كالماء .
اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ۳۲، ط: المكتبة العلمية الهداية كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۵۲، ط: رحمانیه
(41) Indeed, whatever is a tool of purification must itself be pure. Translation: A thing that is a tool for purification must itself be pure. Explanation: The author of Hidayah intends by this principle that the thing with which tayammum is performed must itself be pure. For the one performing tayammum, earth is the tool of purification. Therefore, just as water is a tool of purification and is pure in itself, similarly earth must also be pure in itself. And the sleeper according to Abu Hanifa is legally able, and the one fearing a wild animal is legally incapable, and the difference between the sleeper and the one in fear is that sleep during travel in a way that one is unaware of water is rare, especially in a way that wakefulness indicating water does not intervene, so his sleep was not considered, and he is treated like one awake legally. al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 24. al-Hidayah, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 52. And tayammum is only performed with pure earth (sa'id tahir) because 'tayyib' mentioned in His statement (sa'idan tayyiban) means pure by consensus of the text. Indeed, the purity of earth is a condition according to the four Imams. And from Dawud, if the earth is changed by impurity, tayammum with it is not permissible; if it is not changed, it is permissible. And it is permissible to perform tayammum with used earth according to us. [al-Binayah, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 550] And tayammum is only performed with pure earth because 'tayyib' means pure, and because it is a tool of purification, so it must be pure in itself like water. al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 32. al-Hidayah, Book of Taharah, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 52.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the condition of the medium used in tayammum. The principle is that anything used as an instrument for purification (such as earth for tayammum or water for wudu) must itself be pure. The author of al-Hidayah explains that just as water must be pure to be used for wudu, so too must earth be pure for tayammum. The text then provides a lengthy supporting quotation from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and al-Binayah, which references the Quranic verse 'sa'idan tayyiban' (pure earth) and notes that there is consensus that 'tayyib' means pure (tahir). It also mentions an opinion from Dawud al-Zahiri distinguishing between changed and unchanged earth, but the Hanafi position (followed by the four schools) requires pure earth regardless. Additionally, the passage includes a side note about the sleeper and the one fearing a wild animal, which reinforces the earlier principle about legal ability versus real inability.

Key Terms
آلة التطهير (ālāt al-taṭhīr): The instrument or medium used for purification, such as water for wudu or earth for tayammum.
صعيد طاهر (ṣaʿīd ṭāhir): Pure earth or soil that is free from najasah, used for tayammum.
طيب (ṭayyib): In the Quranic context, interpreted as 'pure' (tahir) by consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Quranic phrase 'sa'idan tayyiban' interpreted as 'pure earth'
B) A hadith from the Prophet
C) Consensus of the companions
D) Analogy with water

Key Takeaway
The instrument of purification must itself be pure; for tayammum, the earth must be pure (tahir) based on the Quranic command of 'sa'idan tayyiban'.

Predominant Opinion is Like Certainty
States the legal maxim that predominant opinion has the force of certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim 'ghalib al-ra'y k'al-mutahaqqiq' and apply it to a fiqh scenario from the chapter of Taharah.

Core Idea
A strong probability in Hanafi fiqh carries the weight of certainty for practical rulings.

This lesson introduces a core Hanafi legal maxim that bridges the gap between absolute certainty and practical necessity. The maxim states that a predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y) is treated as certainty (mutahaqqiq) when absolute certainty is unattainable. This principle is frequently invoked in Taharah and other chapters to determine obligations based on strong probability.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim in Arabic and English
Write the maxim word for word, then provide a literal translation.
2
Define the key terms
Explain 'ghalib al-ra'y' as a strong prevailing opinion based on evidence, and 'mutahaqqiq' as certain knowledge.
Distinguish ghalib al-ra'y from mere doubt (shakk) or whim (hawa).
3
Identify the scope of application
Note that this maxim applies across many fiqh chapters, particularly where objective certainty is impossible, such as in tayammum, impurities, and timings.
4
Apply to a Taharah scenario
Consider a traveller who has a strong belief that water is available within reach. According to the maxim, this predominant opinion obligates him to find water before performing tayammum.
The maxim does not apply to mere suspicion; it requires a genuine predominant opinion.
5
Recognize exceptions
The maxim has limits: it cannot override explicit textual rulings or consensus, and it does not apply in matters requiring absolute certainty (e.g., rulings on ritual purity for acts of worship).
Further details are available in usul al-fiqh texts.

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qa'idah) that a predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y) is treated as certainty (mutahaqqaq) in the Hanafi school. This maxim is often applied in issues where certainty is not possible, and the law relies on strong probability. For example, in matters of tayammum, if a person has a strong belief that water is available, it may affect the ruling. The explanation in the text (cut off) likely provides examples.

Key Terms
غالب الرأي (ghālib al-ra'y): Predominant opinion or strong probability; a legally recognized degree of certainty for practical rulings.
المتحقق (al-mutaḥaqqiq): That which is certain and established as fact.

Principles of Tayammum: Tool Purity, Dominant Opinion, and Certainty
Explaining three Hanafi principles about tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi principles governing tayammum (tool purity, dominant opinion as certainty, and irreversibility of established inability) and apply them to determine the ruling on delaying prayer when water is hoped for.

Core Idea
The tool of purification must be pure; dominant opinion is like certainty; established inability is only removed by equal certainty.

This passage from Usul al-Hidayah lays down three foundational legal maxims (qawa'id) that govern the validity and timing of tayammum. Understanding these principles is essential for correctly applying the rules of purification when water is absent or feared. The passage also illustrates an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a person who has a strong hope of finding water must delay their prayer or merely is recommended to do so.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three principles
Locate each of the three principles in the Arabic text: (41) the tool of purification must be pure, (42) dominant opinion is like certainty, (43) inability established in reality is not removed except by equal certainty.
These are numbered in the original text, making them easy to isolate.
2
Understand the proof for tool purity
The author cites the Quranic phrase 'صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا' (pure earth) and explains that 'tayyib' is interpreted as 'tahir' by consensus. Note also the cross-madhhab views, including Dawud al-Zahiri's position.
Purity of the earth is a condition (shart) for tayammum, analogous to water.
3
Analyze the principle 'dominant opinion is like certainty'
This principle is illustrated by the examples of the sleeping person and the one fleeing a wild beast. It is also used to justify action upon solitary hadith. The author then applies it to the dispute about delaying prayer.
This principle is a key tool in Hanafi usul for weighing evidence.
4
Examine the principle of established inability
Once inability to find water is established in reality, its legal effect (permission for tayammum) persists until certainty of ability arises. Mere hope does not remove it.
This complements the previous principle and limits its application.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The zahir al-riwaya holds delaying prayer as mustahabb; the two shaykhs (in non-zahir narrations) hold it as wajib. The mufta bihi is the zahir al-riwaya position, as affirmed by al-Muhit.
The key difference is whether dominant opinion removes the established inability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(41) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ طَهَارَتِهِ فِي نَفْسِهِ. (42) إِنَّ غَالِبَ الرَّأْيِ كَالْمُتَحَقَّقِ. وَالنَّائِمُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا وَخَائِفُ السَّبُعِ عَاجِزٌ حُكْمًا، وَالْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ النَّائِمِ وَالْخَائِفِ أَنَّ النَّوْمَ فِي حَالَةِ السَّفَرِ عَلَى وَجْهِ لَا يَشْعُرُ بِالْمَاءِ نَادِرٌ خُصُوصًا عَلَى وَجْهِ لَا يَتَخَلَّلُهُ الْيَقَظَةُ الْمُشْعِرَةُ بِالْمَاءِ فَلَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ نَوْمُهُ كَالْيَقْطَانِ حُكْمًا. ولا يتيمم إلا بصعيد طاهر لأن الطيب المذكور فى قَوْله تَعَالَى: (صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا) أريد به الطاهر في النص بالإجماع، إذ طهارة التراب شرط عند الأئمة الأربعة، وعن داود والتراب إذا تغير بالنجاسة لا يجوز التيمم به، وإن لم يتغير جاز، ويجوز التيمم بالتراب المستعمل عندنا. ولا يجوز التيمم إلا بالصعيد الطاهر لأن الطيب أريد به الطاهر، ولأنه آلة التطهير، فلابد من طهارته فى نفسه كالماء. (43) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا يَزُولُ حُكْمُهُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ. وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِرَاجِى الْمَاءِ تَأْخِيرُ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَى آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ فِي ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ لِيَقَعَ الْآدَاءُ بِأَكْمَلِ الطَّهَارَتَيْنِ لَكِنْ لَا يُبَالِغُ فِي التَّأْخِيرِ لِئَلَّا تَقَعَ الصَّلَاةُ فِي وَقْتِ الْكَرَاهَةِ. وَعَنْ الشَّيْخَيْنِ فِي غَيْرِ رِوَايَةِ الْأُصُولِ أَنَّ التَّأْخِيرَ حَتُم لِأَنَّ غَالِبَ الرَّأْيِ كَالْمُتَحَقِّقِ وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ الْعَجْزَ ثَابِتٌ حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا يَزُولُ حُكْمُهُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ، وَفِيهِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ بِدُونِ الرَّجَاءِ لَا يُؤَخِّرُ هَذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ كَمَا فِي الْمُحِيطِ. لأن غالب الرأى كالمتحقق ولهندا وجب العمل بخبر الواحد، والقياس يؤيده، قال الله تعالى: (فَامْتَحِنُوهُنَّ اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِإِيمَانِهِنَّ فَإِنْ عَلِمْتُمُوهُنَّ مُؤْمِنَاتٍ فَلَا تَرْجِعُوهُنَّ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ) علق عندم الرد إليهم بالعلم بكونهن مؤمنات، والعلم بذلك لا يكون إلا لغالب الرأى وهو كالثابت حقيقة.
(41) Indeed, whatever is a tool of purification, its own purity is necessary. (42) Indeed, dominant opinion is like certainty. And the sleeping person according to Abu Hanifa is considered capable (finding water) estimatively, and the one fearing a wild beast is incapable by legal ruling. The difference between the sleeping and the fearing is that sleep during travel in a manner that one does not perceive water is rare, especially in a manner that wakefulness that informs of water does not interrupt it, so his sleep is not considered like wakefulness legally. And one may not perform tayammum except with pure earth because 'tayyib' mentioned in His statement {pure earth} means pure in the text by consensus, since the purity of dust is a condition according to the four Imams, and from Dawud (al-Zahiri) that if dust is changed by impurity, tayammum with it is not permissible, and if not changed, it is permissible, and tayammum with used earth is permissible according to us. And tayammum is not permissible except with pure earth because 'tayyib' means pure, and because it is a tool of purification, so its own purity is necessary like water. (43) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, its ruling is not removed except by certainty equal to it. And it is recommended for one hoping for water to delay prayer to the end of the time in the apparent narration so that the performance occurs with the most complete of the two purifications, but he should not be excessive in delay lest the prayer fall in a disliked time. And from the two Shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in other than the principal narrations that delay is obligatory because dominant opinion is like certainty. The aspect of the apparent (narration) is that inability is established in reality, so its ruling is not removed except by certainty equal to it, and in it is an indication that without hope one does not delay; this is the correct view as in al-Muhit. Because dominant opinion is like certainty, and hence action upon a solitary report became obligatory, and analogy supports it. Allah said: {Examine them; Allah knows best their faith. If you know them to be believers, then do not return them to the disbelievers} He conditioned the prohibition of returning them on knowledge of their being believers, and knowledge of that is not achieved except by dominant opinion, and it is like established in reality.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage from Usool al-Hidayah presents three key Hanafi principles (qawa'id) related to tayammum, expanding on the Hidayah's text. The first principle (41) states that any tool used for purification must itself be pure. This is applied to tayammum: the earth (sa'eed) used must be pure (tahir). The proof is the Quranic phrase 'sa'eedan tayyiban' where 'tayyib' is interpreted by consensus as 'tahir'. This aligns with the four schools, though Dawud al-Zahiri held that earth visibly contaminated by najasah is impermissible, but if the change is not apparent, it is allowed. The Hanafi school also permits tayammum with used earth (turab musta'mal). The principle is analogized to water, which must be pure to purify others.

The second principle (42) establishes that a dominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y) is legally treated as certainty (mutahaqqaq). This is crucial for determining when tayammum is allowed. If one hopes to find water later, waiting is recommended (mustahabb) in the zahir al-riwaya, but the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in non-zahir narrations hold it obligatory (hatam) because dominant opinion of finding water is like actual certainty. The passage also gives an example: a sleeping person is considered able to find water (if water is nearby) only if waking is likely; a person fleeing from a wild beast is legally incapable even if water might be present, because his situation prevents him.

The third principle (43) complements the second: once inability (‘ajz) is established as a fact, its legal effect (permission to do tayammum) continues until certainty of ability arises. Thus, if one is sure no water is present, he may do tayammum at the start. But if the absence is uncertain and he has a dominant hope of finding water, he should wait. The text then quotes a Quranic verse (al-Mumtahanah 60:10) to support that dominant opinion suffices for legal rulings (like knowing a woman's faith). The overall lesson is that Hanafi fiqh balances certainty and probability, using istihsan and qiyas, with the mufta bihi being the zahir al-riwaya position that waiting is recommended but not obligatory, unless the hope is very strong.

Key Terms
آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ (ālat al-taṭhīr): The tool used for purification, such as water or earth for tayammum.
غَالِبَ الرَّأْيِ (ghālib al-ra’y): A strong preponderant opinion based on evidence, treated as certainty in legal rulings.
الْمُتَحَقَّقِ (al-mutaḥaqqaq): That which is established as certain or actual, as opposed to merely probable.
الْعَجْزَ (al-‘ajz): Inability to perform an obligation due to lack of means, here the absence of water.
يَقِينِ (yaqīn): Certainty that is legally sufficient to remove a previous certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle 'غَالِبَ الرَّأْيِ كَالْمُتَحَقَّقِ', what is the ruling for a person who has a dominant hope of finding water before the end of the prayer time?
A) He must perform tayammum immediately without waiting.
B) He should delay prayer to the end of the time, and this is obligatory according to the two shaykhs in non-zahir riwaya, but only recommended in the zahir al-riwaya.
C) He must wait until he finds water, even if the time expires.
D) He may choose to delay or not; it is indifferent (mubah).

Key Takeaway
The three principles together ensure that tayammum is valid when water is truly absent, but a dominant hope of water only makes waiting recommended, not obligatory, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Dominant Probability Like Certainty in Tayammum
Explains principle ghalabat al-zann ka al-mutahaqqiq with tayammum example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that dominant probability (ghalabat al-zann) is treated like certainty in the context of tayammum when hoping for water, and distinguish between the Zahir al-Riwayah and Sahibayn positions.

Core Idea
Dominant probability acts like certainty in law, but a certain inability yields only to equal certainty.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi principle through a concrete example from tayammum: if water is absent but one has a dominant expectation of finding it later, does the certainty of current inability persist? The author of Al-Hidayah uses this case to clarify how ghalabat al-zann functions as a legal proxy for yaqin, and why the school's relied-upon position treats a mere hope differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Understand the situation: a person lacks water for wudu but has a strong hope (significant probability) of finding water before the prayer time ends. Determine whether tayammum is permissible now or must wait.
The scenario hinges on the strength of the probability.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Recall that in Zahir al-Riwayah, delaying is recommended (mustahab); according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn, in non-Zahir al-Riwayah), delaying is obligatory (hatm).
This intra-madhhab ikhtilaf is the core of the lesson.
3
Trace the dalil for each position
The Sahibayn argue from the principle 'ghalabat al-zann ka al-mutahaqqiq' (dominant probability is like certainty) – the hope itself is a strong indicator that water will be found, so tayammum is not permitted. The Zahir al-Riwayah position counters that inability is already certain, and certainty can only be removed by equal certainty, not probability.
The Quranic verse (60:10) is cited to show that in some acts, dominant probability suffices for obligation (khabar al-wahid) but does not undo a certain status.
4
Apply the principle: inability vs. hope
The text states: 'When inability is factually established, its ruling is not removed except by an equal certainty.' So the current inability is certain; a mere hope (even dominant) does not erase that certainty. Therefore, tayammum remains valid until water is actually known.
This is the relied-upon view in the school.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the Sahibayn, a person must wait and cannot perform tayammum early; if he does, he must repeat the prayer. Under the mufta bihi view, he may perform tayammum early but it is better to delay.
Both views agree that the goal is to pray with the most complete purification.

مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۴۳، ط: دار إحياء التراث]
( لأن غالب الرأى كالمتحقق ولهندا وجب العمل بخبر الواحد، والقياس يؤيده،قال الله تعالى: (فَامْتَحِنُوهُنَّ اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِإِيمَانِهِنَّ فَإِنْ عَلِمْتُمُوهُنَّ مُؤْمِنَاتٍ فَلَا تَرْجِعُوهُنَّ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ) علق عندم الرد إليهم بالعلم بكونهن مؤمنات، والعلم بذلك لا يكون إلا لغالب الرأى وهو كالثابت حقيقة
[ البناية : كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۵۵۴، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
الهداية: كتاب الطهارات، باب التيمم، ج ۱ ص ۵۲، ط: رحمانیه
The author of Al-Hidayah mentioned an example to explain this principle: If water is not present and there is hope that it will be found by the end of the prayer time, then in such a case it is recommended (mustahab) to delay the prayer until the end of the time. But if there is no hope, then one should not delay unnecessarily. However, in a non-Zahir al-Riwayah transmission from the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is narrated that if there is hope of finding water, then in that case delaying the prayer is obligatory (lazim). On this, while mentioning the principle, they say that dominant probability is like certainty. If there is hope and dominant assumption of finding water, then in that case one should not perform tayammum but rather delay the prayer until the end of the time, just as tayammum is not permissible when water is present, similarly in the case of hope of finding water, tayammum is not permissible; rather, one should wait until the end of the time and delay the prayer. (43) Indeed, when inability is established as a reality, its ruling is not removed except by an equal certainty. Translation: When inability is factually established, its ruling is not removed except by an equal certainty. And it is recommended for one who hopes for water to delay the prayer until the end of the time in Zahir al-Riwayah so that the performance happens with the more complete of the two purifications, but he should not exaggerate in delay so that the prayer does not fall in the disliked time. And from the two shaykhs in non-Zahir al-Riwayah that delay is obligatory because dominant opinion is like certainty. The face of the apparent view is that inability is established as a reality so its ruling is not removed except by an equal certainty, and in it is an indication that without hope he does not delay; this is the correct view as in Al-Muhit. [Majma' al-Anhur: Book of Purification, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 43, Dar Ihya al-Turath] (Because dominant opinion is like certainty, and for this reason action upon khabar al-wahid is obligatory, and analogy supports it. Allah said: 'So examine them; Allah is most knowing of their faith. And if you know them to be believers, then do not return them to the disbelievers.' He attached the prohibition of returning them to knowledge of their being believers, and that knowledge is only through dominant opinion, which is as if factually established.) [Al-Binayah: Book of Purification, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 554, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah; Al-Hidayah: Book of Purifications, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 52, Rahmaniyyah]
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal principle of ghalabat al-zann (dominant probability) being equivalent to certainty (mutahaqqiq) in the context of tayammum when one hopes to find water. The author of Usool-e-Hidayah explains that the master of Hidayah used an example: if water is absent but one hopes to find it by the end of the prayer time, the ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah is that it is mustahab (recommended) to delay the prayer to the end of the time to perform it with the more complete purification (wudu with water). However, if there is no hope, one should not delay. In a non-Zahir al-Riwayah transmission from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two shaykhs), delaying is obligatory (hatm) because dominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) is like actual certainty. The text then presents the principle that inability (ajz) when factually established is only removed by an equal certainty (yaqin mithlihi). This is the basis for the Zahir al-Riwayah position: since the inability to find water is certain, mere doubt (hope) does not remove it. The passage also cites the Quranic verse from Surah al-Mumtahanah (60:10) as evidence that in legal matters, knowledge based on dominant probability is treated as certainty, similar to the acceptance of ahadith reports. The commentary clarifies that this principle is applied in various fiqh issues, such as acting upon khabar al-wahid.

Key Terms
ظن غالب (ghalabat al-zann): Dominant probability or overwhelming assumption that something is true, based on indications.
متحقق (mutahaqqiq): Factually established or certain; having the status of a reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling for someone who hopes to find water before the end of the prayer time?
A) He must perform tayammum immediately.
B) He must delay the prayer until the end of the time (obligatory).
C) It is recommended for him to delay the prayer until the end of the time.
D) He can choose between tayammum or waiting.

Key Takeaway
When inability to find water is certain, dominant probability of finding it later does not remove that certainty in the relied-upon Hanafi view.
