The Maxim of Certainty: Tayammum Ruling Persists Until Certainty of Water
States principle that real inability is only removed by equal certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'ma thabata bi yaqin la yartafi‘ illa bi yaqin mithlihi' and apply it to the ruling of tayammum when lack of water is certain.

Core Idea
A ruling established by certainty is only removed by equal certainty, not by doubt or probability.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal maxim that governs many rulings in fiqh: certainty (yaqin) is only removed by certainty of the same level. The specific context is tayammum (dry ablution) when a person is certain that water is unavailable. Understanding this maxim prevents confusion about when tayammum remains valid and when it becomes void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum performed due to inability to find water. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah).
This permission is a concession (rukhsah) for those who are certain of the absence of water.
2
State the certainty of inability
The inability (ajz) is established as a factual reality (haqiqatan) through certainty (yaqin).
This certainty comes from actual knowledge of water's absence, not from mere assumption.
3
Introduce the legal maxim
The maxim: 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يزول إلا بيقين مثله' – what is established by certainty is not removed except by equal certainty.
This is a general usul principle that applies to all fiqh rulings based on certainty.
4
Apply the maxim to the ruling of tayammum
Since the permissibility of tayammum is established by certainty, it can only be removed by certainty (yaqin mithlihi) that water is available.
Therefore, mere hope or strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) of water does not invalidate the tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح : ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پانی نہ ملنے کی صورت میں حقیقتا بجز ثابت ہے اور اس شخص کے لئے تیتم کر کے نماز پڑھنے کی گنجائش ہے، لہذا جب پانی نہ ملنے سے حقیقتاً ثابت ہے تو جب تک حقیقی اور یقینی طور پر پانی نہ مل جائے اس وقت تک یہ بجز ختم نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ حقیقتاً ثابت ہونے والی چیزوں کے متعلق ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ مَا ثَبَتَ بِيَقِينِ لَا يَرْتَفِعُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ ، یعنی جو چیز یقین سے ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ یقین ہی سے ختم ہوتی ہے اس کے علاوہ سے نہیں ہوتی ، اس لئے صورت مسئلہ میں بھی جب تک یقینی طور پر پانی دستیاب ہونے کا علم نہیں ہو گا اس وقت تک تیم کا حکم باقی اور برقرار رہے گا۔
ووجه ظاهر الرواية أن العجز ثابت حقيقة فلا يزول حكمه إلا بيقين مثله.
Explanation: The proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that in the case of not finding water, inability is factually established, and for that person there is a concession to perform tayammum and pray. Therefore, when inability is factually established from not finding water, as long as water is not actually and certainly found, this inability will not be removed. This is because the rule regarding things established by certainty is: 'What is established by certainty is not removed except by an equal certainty.' That is, a thing established by certainty only ends by certainty, not by anything else. Hence, in the subject matter, as long as there is no certain knowledge of water being available, the ruling of tayammum remains and continues. And the face of the apparent narration is that inability is established as a reality, so its ruling is not removed except by an equal certainty.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage provides a commentary on the principle that forms the basis of the Zahir al-Riwayah position regarding tayammum when hoping for water. It explains the legal maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يزول إلا بيقين مثله' (What is established by certainty is only removed by an equal certainty). The context is that when a person is certain that water is absent (inability to find water), the ruling of tayammum becomes permissible. This certainty of inability remains in effect until there is actual certainty that water is present. Mere doubt or hope (ghalabat al-zann) that water might be found does not remove the established certainty of inability. The commentator emphasizes that the inability (ajz) is a factual reality (haqiqatan) and its legal effect (hukm) persists unless another certainty arises. Therefore, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, one may perform tayammum with the certainty of inability, and the prayer is valid. If one delays hoping for water, it is only recommended, not obligatory, because the established ruling of inability remains until actual water is found with certainty.

Key Terms
عجز (ajz): Inability or incapacity to find water, which is a factual reality that permits tayammum.
یقین (yaqin): Certainty; a state of sure knowledge that removes doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Dominant probability of water
B) Certainty of water availability
C) Passing of time
D) A new doubt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds that yaqin (certainty) can only be removed by yaqin mithlihi (equal certainty), so tayammum remains valid despite doubt about water.

No Ability Without Knowledge: The Principle and Its Application to Tayammum
States the Hanafi principle that ability requires knowledge, with application to forgotten water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that ability requires knowledge and apply it to the case of a traveler who forgets water.

Core Idea
Forgetting water removes legal ability to use it, so tayammum is valid and prayer is not repeated.

The Hanafi school holds that legal ability (qudrah) to use water is conditional upon knowledge (ilm) of its presence. This lesson examines the principle 'لا قدرة بدون العلم' as cited by the author of Al-Hidayah to justify the ruling of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Through the example of a traveler who forgets water in his saddlebag, we will see how this principle operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the principle
Learn the Arabic maxim 'لا قدرة بدون العلم' and its meaning: 'No ability without knowledge.' This is a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh.
Commit it to memory as a key legal maxim.
2
Understand the scenario
Consider a traveler who places water in his saddlebag, forgets it, and then performs tayammum and prays. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not need to repeat the prayer.
The scenario illustrates the principle's application.
3
Apply the principle
Since he lacked knowledge (ilm) of the water's presence, he did not have legal ability (qudrah) to use it. Therefore, his tayammum was valid and the prayer stands without repetition.
This is the direct legal consequence of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَا قُدْرَةَ بِدُون الْعِلْمِ .
ترجمہ: بغیر علم کے قدرت حاصل نہیں ہوتی۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول کو ذکر کر کے حضرات طرفین کا مسلک ثابت کیا ہے اور
اسے بطور دلیل کے ذکر کیا ہے۔ طرفین کے ہاں اگر مسافر پانی کجاوے میں رکھ کر بھول گیا اور تیم کر کے نماز پڑھ لی تو اس ا پر نماز کا اعادہ واجب نہیں ہے ، وجہ یہ ہے کہ پانی پر قادر ہونا بغیر علم کے نہیں ہوسکتا اور اس کو علم بھی نہیں ہے اور اصول ہے کہ بغیر علم کے قدرت حاصل نہیں ہوتی ، تو جب اس کو معلوم ہی نہیں تو قدرت نہ ہوئی اور جب قدرت نہیں تو اسے پانی حاصل بھی نہیں ہوا، اور پانی حاصل نہ ہونے کی
حاشية الطحطاوي على مراقى الفلاح كتاب الطهارة، باب التيمم، ج ا ص ١٢٢ ، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ]
There is no ability without knowledge. Translation: Ability is not obtained without knowledge. Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah mentioned the principle and established the position of the two parties (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and mentioned it as a proof. According to both, if a traveler placed water in his saddlebag and forgot it, and performed tayammum and prayed, then repeating the prayer is not obligatory for him. The reason is that having ability over water cannot be without knowledge, and he had no knowledge. And the principle is that ability is not obtained without knowledge. So when he had no knowledge, there was no ability, and when there was no ability, he did not obtain water. And due to not obtaining water... [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi ala Maraqi al-Falah, Book of Purification, Chapter of Tayammum, vol. 1 p. 122, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah]
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage introduces the legal principle 'لا قدرة بدون العلم' (No ability without knowledge). The author states this as a principle that the master of Hidayah used to establish the position of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The example given is of a traveler who has water in his saddlebag but forgets it. He performs tayammum and prays. According to the two shaykhs, he is not required to repeat the prayer. The reasoning is that ability (qudrah) to use water is conditional upon knowledge (ilm) of its presence. Since he forgot, he had no knowledge, and therefore he was not legally capable of using water. Hence, his tayammum was valid and his prayer is not to be repeated. This principle is from the usul (foundations) of the school and is cited here to justify the ruling in the margin (hashiyah) of Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah. The commentary explains that the lack of knowledge negates the existence of power over water, and thus tayammum is proper.

Key Terms
قدرت (qudrah): Legal ability or capability to perform an act, here specifically the ability to use water.
علم (ilm): Knowledge or awareness of the presence of water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'لا قدرة بدون العلم', if a traveler forgets that he has water, performs tayammum and prays, what is the ruling?
A) He must repeat the prayer because water was available.
B) He does not need to repeat the prayer because he lacked knowledge.
C) He must repeat only if he had a doubt.
D) He must repeat after the time ends.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle 'لا قدرة بدون العلم' means that legal ability to use water depends on knowledge; forgetfulness makes tayammum valid and obviates the need to repeat prayer.

Certainty and Doubt in Tayammum: Persistence of a Valid Excuse
Explaining the application of the legal maxim to tayammum's persistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the legal maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرتفع إلا بيقين مثله' to determine the validity of tayammum when water is uncertainly present.

Core Idea
Tayammum remains valid until water's presence is certain—doubt does not break established inability.

This passage from the Zahir al-Riwayah demonstrates a key application of the foundational maxim 'What is established by certainty is not removed by doubt.' The Hanafi school uses this principle to preserve the validity of acts of worship once a sound basis is established. Here, the focus is on the persistence of tayammum: a valid excuse (inability to find water) continues until it is removed with equal certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the established certainty
When a person performs tayammum due to inability to find water, that inability (ajz) is a real state established with certainty at that moment.
The source text says: 'العجز ثابت حقيقة'.
2
Recognize the legal consequence
From this established inability, the Shari'ah permits tayammum and grants it the ruling of taharah. This ruling is now fixed.
3
Apply the legal maxim
The maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرتفع إلا بيقين مثله' dictates that a certainty-based ruling is only removed by an equal certainty. Doubt or suspicion does not suffice.
The maxim is cited in the source: 'الضابطۃ... مَا ثَبَتَ بِيَقِينِ لَا يَرْتَفِعُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ'.
4
Derive the specific tayammum ruling
Thus, as long as water's availability is not known with certainty, the tayammum remains valid. The person may continue to pray with it.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح : ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پانی نہ ملنے کی صورت میں حقیقتا بجز ثابت ہے اور اس شخص کے لئے تیتم کر کے نماز پڑھنے کی گنجائش ہے، لہذا جب پانی نہ ملنے سے حقیقتاً ثابت ہے تو جب تک حقیقی اور یقینی طور پر پانی نہ مل جائے اس وقت تک یہ بجز ختم نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ حقیقتاً ثابت ہونے والی چیزوں کے متعلق ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ مَا ثَبَتَ بِيَقِينِ لَا يَرْتَفِعُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ ، یعنی جو چیز یقین سے ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ یقین ہی سے ختم ہوتی ہے اس کے علاوہ سے نہیں ہوتی ، اس لئے صورت مسئلہ میں بھی جب تک یقینی طور پر پانی دستیاب ہونے کا علم نہیں ہو گا اس وقت تک تیم کا حکم باقی اور برقرار رہے گا۔ ووجه ظاهر الرواية أن العجز ثابت حقيقة فلا يزول حكمه إلا بيقين مثله.
Explanation: The proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that when water is not found, inability is established in reality, and there is scope for that person to perform tayammum and pray. Therefore, when inability is established due to the non-finding of water in reality, it will not end until water is actually and certainly found, because the rule regarding things established with certainty is: 'What is established by certainty is not removed except by certainty equal to it.' So in this case, as long as the availability of water is not known with certainty, the ruling of tayammum remains and persists. And the position of Zahir al-Riwayah is that inability is established in reality, so its ruling does not cease except by equal certainty.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Zahir al-Riwayah. It explains the application of the famous legal maxim 'What is established by certainty is not removed by doubt' to the case of tayammum. According to the Hanafi school, when a person legitimately performs tayammum due to inability to find water, that tayammum remains valid until water is actually and certainly found. Mere doubt or suspicion about water's presence does not invalidate it. The maxim ensures stability in acts of worship: once a valid excuse is established, it persists until its removal is equally certain.

Key Terms
عجز (ajz): inability to use water, the excuse allowing tayammum
مَا ثَبَتَ بِيَقِينِ لَا يَرْتَفِعُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ (mā thabata bi-yaqīnin lā yarta fiʿu illā bi-yaqīnin mithlihi): A legal maxim: what is established by certainty is not removed except by equal certainty
تیمم (tayammum): dry ablution with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler performs tayammum and later doubts whether water has become available, but is not certain, what is the status of his tayammum according to Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) It becomes invalid immediately.
B) It remains valid until he is certain water is available.
C) He must repeat both tayammum and prayer.
D) He must perform tayammum again if he suspects water.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists that tayammum remains valid until water's availability is known with certainty, applying the maxim: certainty is not removed by doubt.

No Ability Without Knowledge: The Case of Forgotten Water
Explaining the principle that ability requires knowledge, applied to a traveler who forgets water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a traveler forgets water and explain why the Hanafi school considers the prayer valid using the principle 'la qudrata bi-dun al-ilm'.

Core Idea
If you forget water, you are not legally able to use it — your tayammum is valid.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi legal principle: ability requires knowledge. The Hidayah applies this to a traveler who forgets water in his saddle. Understanding this principle helps you see how classical scholars reason from usul to furu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A traveler performs tayammum and prays after forgetting water. The ruling according to the Sahibayn is that the prayer is valid and does not require repetition.
2
Locate the dalil (principle)
The proof is the maxim 'لا قدرة بدون العلم' (No ability without knowledge). This is a rational proof (qiyas) based on the nature of legal capacity.
The maxim is implicitly derived from the Qur'anic principle that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.
3
Understand the illa
The effective cause (illa) is that legal ability (qudrah) for using water requires knowledge ('ilm) of its presence. Without knowledge, the person is not considered capable.
This is a condition for taklif (legal responsibility).
4
Apply to the case
Since the traveler lacks knowledge of the water, he is not legally able to use it. Therefore, he may perform tayammum, and the prayer is valid.
The principle overrides the objective existence of water.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa may have a different view. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require repetition even if water was forgotten.
Later fatwas adopt the Sahibayn's view as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۴) لَا قُدْرَةَ بِدُون الْعِلْمِ . ) ترجمہ: بغیر علم کے قدرت حاصل نہیں ہوتی۔ تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول کو ذکر کر کے حضرات طرفین کا مسلک ثابت کیا ہے اور اسے بطور دلیل کے ذکر کیا ہے۔ طرفین کے ہاں اگر مسافر پانی کجاوے میں رکھ کر بھول گیا اور تیم کر کے نماز پڑھ لی تو اس ا پر نماز کا اعادہ واجب نہیں ہے ، وجہ یہ ہے کہ پانی پر قادر ہونا بغیر علم کے نہیں ہوسکتا اور اس کو علم بھی نہیں ہے اور اصول ہے کہ بغیر علم کے قدرت حاصل نہیں ہوتی ، تو جب اس کو معلوم ہی نہیں تو قدرت نہ ہوئی اور جب قدرت نہیں تو اسے پانی حاصل بھی نہیں ہوا، اور پانی حاصل نہ ہونے کی صورت میں تیم جائز ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں پر بھی تیم جائز اور نماز درست ہو جائے گی۔
(44) There is no ability without knowledge. Translation: Ability is not acquired without knowledge. Explanation: The author of Hidayah mentioned this principle and proved the position of the two (Sahibayn) and mentioned it as evidence. According to the two, if a traveler places water in his saddlebag and forgets it, then performs tayammum and prays, the repetition of the prayer is not obligatory. The reason is that being able to use water cannot exist without knowledge, and he does not have knowledge. The principle is that ability is not acquired without knowledge. So when he does not know, he has no ability, and when he has no ability, he has not obtained water. In the case of not obtaining water, tayammum is permissible. Hence, here too tayammum is permissible and the prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof based on the principle 'No ability without knowledge'. The proof is for the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). They apply this principle to a traveler who forgets water in his saddlebag. Since he has no knowledge of the water's presence, he is not legally considered capable (qadir) of using it. Therefore, his tayammum is valid and his prayer does not need to be repeated. The principle underscores that legal ability (qudrah) is contingent upon knowledge ('ilm).

Key Terms
قدرة (qudrah): legal ability or capacity, here specifically to use water for purification
علم ('ilm): knowledge, here awareness of the presence of water
وجوب الاعادة (wujūb al-iʿādah): obligation to repeat the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'No ability without knowledge', if a traveler forgets water in his saddlebag and performs tayammum, what is the ruling on his prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and does not require repetition.
C) The tayammum is invalid but the prayer is valid.
D) He must repeat both tayammum and prayer.

Key Takeaway
Legal ability (qudrah) in Hanafi fiqh requires knowledge ('ilm); without knowledge, an action based on necessity like tayammum is valid.

When Exorbitant Price Permits Tayammum
Explaining that harm (exorbitant price) removes the obligation to buy water for wudu, allowing tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for purchasing water from a travel companion and identify when tayammum is permitted, and explain the Hanafi proof using the principle 'Harm is removed'.

Core Idea
Exorbitant financial harm lifts the obligation to buy water for wudu, allowing tayammum.

This lesson explores a specific ruling in the chapter of taharah: when can a traveler perform tayammum even though water is available for purchase? The Hanafi school distinguishes between fair price, minor overcharge, and exorbitant price. Only the last exempts the traveler from buying, based on the overarching principle that the Shariah removes harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is performing tayammum when water is available from a companion. Default: one must ask for water, and if sold at a fair price, one must buy it. Tayammum is invalid.
The default preserves the obligation to use water.
2
Distinguish the three price scenarios
The passage lists: (1) market price, (2) minor fraud (ghaban yasir), (3) exorbitant fraud (ghaban fahish). The ruling for the first two is the same: tayammum is not allowed.
Only the third scenario triggers the exception.
3
Apply the principle 'Harm is removed'
The author uses the principle to argue that exorbitant price constitutes financial harm, which the Shariah removes. Therefore, the obligation to buy water is lifted, and tayammum becomes permissible.
The principle overrides the general obligation to use water.
4
Trace the legal analogy (qiyas)
The reasoning analogizes financial harm to physical harm: just as one is not required to suffer lethal harm for water, one is not required to bear excessive financial loss. Property is as inviolable as life.
This is a qiyas based on the illah of harm.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may obligate purchase even at high prices if affordable. The Hanafi position is based on the broad application of the harm removal principle.
The disagreement is rooted in how much financial sacrifice is required for purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۵) إِنَّ الضَّرَرَ مُسْقِط . ترجمہ: ضر ر کو ساقط کر دیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح : حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر رفیق سفر کے پاس پانی ہو تو حکم یہ ہے کہ تیم کرنے سے قبل اس سے مانگنا ضروری ہے، اگر دیدے تو فبہاور نہ تیم کر کے نماز پڑھے۔ لیکن اگر رفیق سفر پانی قیمتاً دیتا ہے اور مسافر شخص پانی لینے پر قادر ہے، تو اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں: .. و مثل قیمت کے عوض فروخت کرے۔ غبن بیر کے ساتھ فروخت کرے۔ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرے۔ پہلی دونوں صورتوں میں تیم جائز نہیں کیونکہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں وہ پانی لینے پر قادر ہے۔ البتہ تیسری صورت میں تیم جائز ہوگا ، اس تیسری صورت کی وجہ صاحب ہدایہ نے اصولِ مذکورہ سے ذکر کی ہے کہ غبن فاحش برداشت کرنے میں اسے ضرر لاحق ہوگا، حالانکہ اصول ہے کہ ضرر ساقط کیا گیا ہے، اس لئے کہ مسلمان کا مال اسی طرح قابلا حترام ہے جیسا کہ اس کی جان قابلِ احترام ہے اور جان کے سلسلہ میں ضرر ساقط ہے، لہذا مال کا ضرر بھی ساقط ہوگا ، تو غبن
(45) Indeed, harm is removed. Translation: Harm has been set aside. Explanation: The conclusion is that if a travel companion has water, the ruling is that before performing tayammum, one must ask for it. If he gives it, fine; otherwise, perform tayammum and pray. But if the travel companion sells water for a price and the traveler is able to take it, then there are three scenarios: (1) He sells it at the market price. (2) He sells it with a minor fraud. (3) He sells it with an exorbitant fraud. In the first two scenarios, tayammum is not permissible because he is able to obtain water. However, in the third scenario, tayammum is permissible. The author of Hidayah gave the reason for this third scenario using the aforementioned principle: in bearing exorbitant fraud, harm will befall him, whereas the principle is that harm is removed. Because the property of a Muslim is as respectable as his life, and in the matter of life, harm is removed; therefore, harm to property is also removed, so exorbitant fraud...
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage discusses a ruling with proof from the principle 'Harm is removed'. It concerns a traveler who has a companion with water. If the companion sells water at a fair price or with minor fraud, the traveler must buy it and cannot perform tayammum. But if the companion demands an exorbitant price (ghaban fahish), tayammum becomes permissible because having to pay such a price would cause harm, and the Shariah removes harm. The analogy is drawn with the sanctity of life: just as a person is not required to endure lethal harm for water, so too is he not required to endure excessive financial harm to his property.

Key Terms
ضرر (darar): harm, here specifically financial harm from an exorbitant price
غبن فاحش (ghaban fāḥish): exorbitant fraud or price disparity considered unreasonable by custom
تیمم (tayammum): dry ablution as a substitute for wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following scenarios does the Hanafi school permit tayammum when water is available for purchase from a travel companion?
A) When the seller gives the water for free.
B) When the seller charges the market price.
C) When the seller charges an exorbitant price (ghaban fahish).
D) When the seller charges a slightly inflated price (ghaban yasir).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school removes the obligation to buy water for wudu when the price is exorbitant, based on the principle that harm is removed.
